Reciting Du'a During Wudu: A Recommended Sunnah
Ruling on etiquette of du'a during wudu with proofs from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting du'a during wudu (mustahabb) and explain the proofs from the Sunnah that establish this recommendation.

Core Idea
Reciting du'a during wudu is recommended, not obligatory – the Prophet's action shows virtue, not compulsion.

Wudu is not just a physical act; it is also a spiritual one. The Prophet ﷺ would recite supplications and Quran during his wudu. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on reciting du'a during wudu: is it required or just recommended? We will look at the proofs from hadith and understand why the Hanafis classify it as mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, identify what precise act is being discussed: reciting the reported du'a (ma'thur) during and after wudu. Then note the ruling: the text says it is an 'adab' (etiquette), which the Hanafi scholars classify as mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
The term 'adab' here is a strong indicator of recommendation.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Two hadiths are cited. The first is the practice of the Prophet ﷺ reciting Quranic verses (Surah Al-Imran:190) during wudu as observed by Ibn Abbas. The second is a hadith promising Paradise for reciting the shahada three times after wudu.
Both hadiths are ahad (single-chain) but authentic.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Indicates the Ruling)
For the first hadith: the Prophet's action is an evidence of permissibility and virtue, but in usul, an action (fi'l) does not indicate obligation unless there is a command (amr). For the second hadith: the promise of reward (targhib) indicates recommendation, not obligation.
Hanafis distinguish between a promise of reward for an act and a command; a promise alone does not make it fard/wajib.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
All madhahib agree that reciting du'a during wudu is recommended. There is no substantial disagreement on the ruling itself, though specific wordings may vary.
This consensus strengthens the ruling but does not change its level.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preferred View)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that reciting du'a during and after wudu is recommended. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute on this point.
The proofs from the Sunnah are clear, and no stronger evidence contradicts them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في آداب الوضوء
بالماثورة (۱۰) والتسمية عند كل عضو (۱۰۷) وادخال خنصره في صماخ اذنيه
تشريح : جس وقت زبان سے نیت کر رہا ہو تو دل بھی اس نیت کے لئے متوجہ ہو ، غافل دل سے نیت نہ کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۰۶) [۶] ماثورہ دعاء پڑھنا۔
تشریح : وضو کرتے وقت حدیث میں جو دعا منقول ہے وہ پڑھنا ادب ہے۔
صلى الله
وجه : (ا) عن عبد الله بن عباس انه رقد عند رسول الله عالم فاستيقظ فتسوک و توضأ و هو يقول ان في خلق السموات و الارض و اختلاف الليل والنهار لأيات لاولى الالباب آیت ۱۹۰ ، سورة آل عمران ) ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب صلاۃ النبی و دعاه باللیل، ص ۳۰۹ نمبر ۱۷۹۹/۷۶۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کے وقت دعاء پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک عن النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من توضأ فاحسن الوضوء ثم قال ثلاث مرات اشهد ان لا اله الا الله وحده لا شریک له و اشهد ان محمدا عبده و رسوله فتح له ثمانية ابواب الجنة من أيها شاء دخل (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما یقال بعد الوضوء ،ص ۶۷ نمبر ۴۶۹ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کے بعد کیا پڑھے۔
Chapter on the etiquettes of wudu. With the reported [du'a] (106) and the tasmiyah at every limb (107) and inserting his little finger into the hollow of his ears (108). Explanation: When one is making intention with the tongue, the heart should also be attentive to that intention; do not make intention with a heedless heart. Translation: (106) [6] Reciting the reported du'a. Explanation: Reciting the du'a that is transmitted in the hadith during wudu is an etiquette. Proof: (1) From Abdullah ibn Abbas that he slept near the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم, then woke up, used the miswak, performed wudu, and was reciting: 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth and the alternation of the night and the day are signs for those of understanding' (Quran 3:190). (Muslim, chapter on the prayer of the Prophet and his supplication at night, p. 309 no. 1799/763). This hadith indicates that he used to recite du'a during wudu. (2) Also in this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Whoever performs wudu and does it well, then says three times: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and His Messenger, the eight gates of Paradise will be opened for him, and he may enter through whichever he wishes.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on what is said after wudu, p. 67 no. 469). This hadith indicates what to recite after wudu.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the etiquette of reciting du'a during wudu. The author begins by listing the etiquettes of wudu, then provides a general note about intention: when verbalizing intention, the heart must also be present. Then he specifies the first etiquette: reciting the reported du'a. He explains that reciting the du'a transmitted in hadith during wudu is an adab (etiquette). He then provides two proofs: first, the practice of Abdullah ibn Abbas observing the Prophet reciting Quranic verses during wudu, specifically Surah Al-Imran verse 190. This shows the permissibility and recommendation of reciting Quran during wudu. Second, a hadith from Anas instructing the recitation of the shahada three times after wudu, promising entry to Paradise. Thus, the passage covers both du'a during and after wudu. In the Hanafi madhhab, reciting du'a during wudu is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. The proofs are authentic ahadith, but they indicate recommendation, not obligation.

Key Terms
ماثورہ (ma'thur): Reported; here it refers to the du'a transmitted in the hadith that is recited during wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on reciting du'a during wudu?
A) It is obligatory (fard)
B) It is recommended (adab/mustahabb)
C) It is permissible (mubah)
D) It is disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
Reciting the reported du'as during and after wudu is a recommended sunnah that brings great reward, but it is not obligatory.

Saying Bismillah at Each Limb During Wudu
Etiquette of saying Bismillah when washing each limb in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on saying Bismillah at each limb during wudu and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Saying Bismillah at each limb is a recommended etiquette that completes the purification of the body.

While the du'a before wudu is one established etiquette, the practice of reciting Bismillah separately when washing each limb is a separate sunnah emphasized by the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson explores the ruling and the hadith proof that encourages this practice for more complete purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Bismillah' when washing each limb during wudu. The passage categorizes it as an adab (etiquette) and the Hanafi school rules it as mustahabb/recommended (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
It is distinct from the du'a recited before wudu.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites a hadith from Abu Huraira: the Prophet ﷺ said that mentioning Allah's name results in complete purification of the whole body, whereas omission limits purification to the washed parts only.
The hadith is narrated by Darqutni, Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The contrast between 'entire body' and 'place of wudu' indicates that tasmiyah increases the scope of purity. This encourages the practice but does not impose an obligation, as the hadith is ahad and does not use a command form.
The Hanafi principle: ahad hadith with praise/reward indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider saying Bismillah at the start of wudu as wajib (obligatory). The Hanafi school disagrees, viewing it as sunnah muakkadah due to the zanni nature of the proof.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if omitted, the Hanafi wudu is still valid; the other school would require it to be repeated.

Source Text

Translation: (107) [7] Reciting Bismillah at the time of washing each limb. Explanation: Reciting the du'a before wudu is a separate etiquette, and reciting Bismillah separately at the time of washing each limb is a separate etiquette; here the same is mentioned. Proof: From Abu Huraira said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Whoever performs wudu and mentions the name of Allah, his entire body becomes purified; and whoever performs wudu and does not mention the name of Allah, nothing is purified except the place of wudu.' (Darqutni, vol. 1, chapter on tasmiyah upon wudu, p. 76 no. 229; Bayhaqi, vol. 1, chapter on tasmiyah upon wudu, p. 74 no. 200; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 1 no. 17)

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the etiquette of saying Bismillah when washing each limb. The author clarifies that there are two distinct recitations: the du'a before wudu (mentioned in the previous point) and the Bismillah at each limb. The proof is a hadith from Abu Huraira indicating that mentioning Allah's name during wudu results in complete purification, while omission limits purification to the washed parts only. In the Hanafi madhhab, saying Bismillah at the start of wudu is sunnah muakkadah, and repeating it at each limb is also recommended. This hadith is cited to encourage the practice.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is obligatory (fard)
B) It is a recommended etiquette (adab)
C) It is forbidden (haram)
D) It is disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
Saying Bismillah at each limb is a recommended sunnah that enhances the spiritual benefit of wudu.

Inserting the Little Finger into Ear Holes During Wudu
Fiqh ruling on recommended finger insertion during ear wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (hukm) of inserting a finger into the ear holes during wudu and identify the sunnah method from the hadith.

Core Idea
Inserting a finger into ear holes during wudu is mustahabb, not obligatory.

This lesson examines the recommended act of inserting a finger into the ear holes while wiping the head during wudu. While the text mentions the little finger, the hadith evidence shows the Prophet (saw) used his index fingers. Understanding the ruling and method is important for correctly performing the sunnah of ear wiping.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the hukm level of inserting the finger into the ear holes: it is mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah), not fard or wajib.
The passage explicitly says 'مستحب ہے' (mustahabb).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb transmitted by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah. This hadith describes the Prophet's wudu.
The text quotes the hadith partially; it mentions using index fingers for inside and thumbs for outside.
3
Analyze the hadith
The hadith explicitly states the Prophet inserted his two index fingers (subbahatayn) into his ears. This shows the recommended method.
The passage notes a discrepancy: the heading says little finger (khinsir) but the hadith says index fingers (subbahatayn). The Hanafi sunnah uses index fingers.
4
Apply the ruling
Determine the sunnah method: wet index fingers and wipe inside of ears, use thumbs to wipe back of ears. This completes the sunnah of ear wiping.
Omitting this does not invalidate wudu but reduces reward.
5
Note the khilaf
Some schools do not consider ear wiping as sunnah at all; Hanafis consider it sunnah muakkadah. This is a legitimate difference.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۱۰۸) [۸] اپنی چھنگلی کو کان کے دونوں سوراخوں میں داخل کرنا۔
تشریح : سر پر سج کرتے وقت دونوں ہاتھ کی انگلیوں کو کان کے سوراخ میں داخل کرنا مستحب ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن عمر و بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده قال ان رجلا اتى النبي الله فقال يا رسول الله ! كيف الطهور ؟ فدعا بماء فى اناء فغسل كفيه ثلاثا ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا ثم غسل ذراعيه ثلاثا ثم مسح برأ رأسه و ادخل اصبعيه السباحتين في اذنيه و مسح بابهامیه علی ظاهر اذنيه و بالسباحتين باطن اذنيه ثم غسل رجليه ثلاثا ثلاثا ثم قال هكذا الوضوء ، فمن زاد على هذا او نقص فقد اساء و ظلم او ظلم و أساء (ابوداود شریف، باب الوضوء ثلا نا ص ۲۹، نمبر ۱۳۵ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب ماجاء فی مسح الاذنین ، ص ۶۴ نمبر ۴۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ شہادت کی انگلی کان میں ڈالتے ۔ لغت : خنصر : ہاتھ کی چھوٹی انگلی ۔ صماخ سوراخ ۔
Translation: (108) [8] Inserting his little finger into both holes of his ears. Explanation: When performing masah of the head, inserting the fingers of both hands into the ear holes is mustahabb (recommended). Proof: (1) From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather said: A man came to the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, how is purification?' He called for water in a vessel and washed his palms three times, then washed his face three times, then washed his forearms three times, then wiped his head and inserted his two index fingers into his ears and wiped the back of his ears with his thumbs and the inside of his ears with his index fingers, then washed his feet three times, then said: 'This is wudu; whoever adds to this or reduces has done wrong and transgressed' (or 'transgressed and done wrong'). (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu three times, p. 29 no. 135; Ibn Majah, chapter on wiping the ears, p. 64 no. 439). This hadith indicates that he inserted the index finger into the ear. Lexicon: khinsir: little finger of the hand; simakh: hole.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the etiquette of wiping the ears during wudu. The author explains that it is mustahabb to insert the little finger into the ear holes while wiping the head. However, the provided hadith actually describes using the index fingers (subbahatayn) for the inside and thumbs for the outside. The author notes the linguistic difference: the text mentions 'khinsir' (little finger) but the hadith mentions 'subbahatayn' (index fingers). This may be a minor discrepancy in the source or a different practice. In Hanafi fiqh, the sunnah is to wipe the ears with the index fingers inside and thumbs outside, as in the hadith. The insertion of the little finger is not specifically mentioned in the hadith, so it might be considered a separate recommendation. The passage also includes lexical definitions: khinsir is the little finger, simakh is the ear hole.

Key Terms
خنصر (khinsir): The little finger of the hand; in this context, the finger inserted into the ear hole.
صماخ (simakh): The ear hole or auditory canal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on inserting the little finger into the ear holes during wudu?
A) It is obligatory (fard)
B) It is recommended (mustahabb)
C) It is forbidden (haram)
D) It is a pillar (rukn)

Key Takeaway
Inserting a finger (preferably the index) into the ear holes during wudu is mustahabb, based on the Prophet's practice; the exact finger is not critical, but the inside should be wiped.

Moving a Ring During Wudu
Ruling on moving a ring during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the ruling for moving a tight ring versus a loose ring during wudu and state the sunnah and mustahabb recommendations.

Core Idea
Moving a tight ring is sunnah; moving a loose ring is mustahabb but not required.

Wudu requires water to reach every part of the limb. A ring can obstruct water. This lesson clarifies the recommended actions for different ring fits, based on the Hanafi position from the sunan of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is moving a ring during wudu. Determine the ruling based on the ring's fit: tight vs loose.
2
Distinguish tight vs loose
For a tight ring, moving it is sunnah (recommended). For a loose ring, moving it is mustahabb (presumed water reaches under it).
The hadith for this is referenced from the Sunan of Wudu.
3
Recall the dalil
The ruling is based on a hadith from the sunan of wudu (not quoted here). The general principle is ensuring water reaches all parts of the limb.
4
Apply the rationale
A tight ring may prevent water from reaching the skin, so movement is sunnah. A loose ring allows water to pass, so movement is only mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۰۹) [۹] کشادہ انگوٹھی کو ہلا دینا۔
تشریح : انگوٹھی تنگ ہو تو ہلا نا سنت ہے، اور کشادہ ہو تو اندازہ ہے کہ اس میں پانی پہنچ ہی گیا ہو گا اس لئے ہلا نا مستحب ہے۔ حدیث سنن وضو میں گزر چکی ہے۔
Translation: (109) [9] Shaking a loose ring. Explanation: If the ring is tight, shaking it is sunnah; and if it is loose, it is presumed that water has already reached under it, so shaking it is mustahabb. The hadith has passed in the Sunan of Wudu.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the etiquette of moving a ring during wudu. The author distinguishes between a tight ring and a loose ring. For a tight ring, moving it is sunnah (recommended) to ensure water reaches under it. For a loose ring, moving it is mustahabb (recommended) because water is presumed to have reached under it already, but shaking it is still good to be thorough. The author mentions that the hadith for this ruling has already been presented earlier in the section on the sunan of wudu. In Hanafi fiqh, ensuring that water reaches all parts of the limb is necessary for the validity of wudu. If a ring is too tight and prevents water from reaching the skin, wudu may be invalid. Therefore, moving the ring is a precautionary measure.

Key Terms
خاتم (khatam): Ring; specifically a finger ring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is sunnah (recommended)
C) It is permissible (mubah)
D) It is disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on moving a ring during wudu depends on its fit: sunnah for tight, mustahabb for loose.

Performing Wudu Before Prayer Time
Ruling with proof on wudu before time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing wudu before prayer time for the unexcused and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Wudu before time is mustahabb for the unexcused; maintaining purity is a sign of faith.

This lesson addresses a recommended practice that reflects the value of prayer. It explains when performing wudu before the prayer time is encouraged and who it applies to. The proof is a hadith emphasizing constant purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu before the time of a prayer enters. The text states it is 'mustahabb' (recommended) for those without a valid excuse.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Thawban (radiyallahu anhu) that 'None maintains purity except a believer.' This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but sufficient for non-obligatory rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith praises consistent purity. Performing wudu before prayer time is a manifestation of that consistency, showing it is a virtuous act.
The indication is general praise, not a direct command.
4
Note the condition
The recommendation is conditional on having no excuse (ghayr ma'dhur). A ma'dhur (excuseful person) is not recommended to do so because it may cause hardship.
The ma'dhur has a special ruling: his wudu is valid until he exits the prayer time or commits a major invalidator.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
There is no significant dispute; all madhhabs agree it is recommended. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
The epistemological weight is from zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the etiquette of performing wudu before the prayer time. The author states that for a person who has no excuse (such as traveling or illness), it is mustahabb (recommended) to perform wudu before the prayer time enters. This is because it demonstrates the importance of prayer and ensures readiness. The proof is a hadith from Thawban that only a believer consistently maintains purity. In Hanafi fiqh, wudu is valid before the time, but its reward is greater when performed close to the prayer. However, for those with a valid excuse (e.g., constant incontinence), it is not recommended because it may lead to difficulty.

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a valid excuse (e.g., chronic illness, incontinence) who cannot maintain wudu; such a person is exempt from this recommendation.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is encouraged but not obligatory. Its performance brings reward, and omission does not bring sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Moving a Ring During Wudu: Sunnah vs Mustahabb
Ruling on moving a ring during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for moving a ring during wudu and differentiate between the sunnah and mustahabb categories.

Core Idea
Moving a tight ring in wudu is sunnah; moving a loose ring is mustahabb.

This lesson addresses a practical issue in wudu: whether one should move a ring to ensure water reaches the skin. The passage provides a clear distinction based on the ring's fit. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the proper level of recommendation in your wudu practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases of ring fit
The passage distinguishes between a tight ring and a loose ring. Determine which case applies to your situation.
2
State the ruling for each case
For a tight ring, moving it is sunnah (recommended). For a loose ring, moving it is mustahabb (recommended but less emphasized).
Sunnah is higher in recommendation than mustahabb.
3
Understand the reasoning
A tight ring may prevent water from reaching the skin, so moving it is sunnah to ensure coverage. A loose ring allows water to seep underneath, so moving it is only mustahabb since water is assumed to have reached.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of avoiding unnecessary burden.
4
Recall the hadith reference
The passage references a hadith on the sunan of wudu that supports this ruling. Although not quoted, it grounds the rule in Prophetic practice.
If you wish, you may look up the specific hadith in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۹) و تحریک خاتمه الواسع

ترجمه : (۱۰۹) [۹] کشادہ انگوٹھی کو ہلا دینا۔

تشریح : انگوٹھی تنگ ہو تو ہلا نا سنت ہے، اور کشادہ ہو تو اندازہ ہے کہ اس میں پانی پہنچ ہی گیا ہو گا اس لئے ہلا نا مستحب ہے۔ حدیث سنن وضو میں گزر چکی ہے۔
(109) And moving the loose ring. Translation: (109) [9] To move a loose ring. Explanation: If the ring is tight, moving it is sunnah; if it is loose, it is assumed that water has already reached under it, so moving it is mustahabb. The hadith on the sunan of wudu has already passed.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the etiquettes of wudu: whether one should move a ring to ensure water reaches the skin. The author distinguishes two cases: if the ring is tight (i.e., fits closely so water cannot easily reach under), moving it is a sunnah (recommended practice) to ensure water reaches the skin. If the ring is loose and it is assumed water has already reached beneath it, moving it is merely mustahabb (recommended but not emphasized). The proof for this is a hadith mentioned earlier in the chapter on the sunan of wudu. This ruling reflects the Hanafi emphasis on ensuring water reaches all parts of the limb while not burdening unnecessarily.

Key Terms
خاتم (khatam): a ring worn on the finger
واسع (wasi'): loose, not tight
تحریک (tahrik): moving, shaking

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for moving a loose ring during wudu according to this passage?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah
C) It is mustahabb
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Moving a tight ring during wudu is sunnah, while moving a loose ring is mustahabb, based on the likelihood of water reaching the skin.

Etiquette of Using Right Hand for Rinsing and Left for Blowing Nose
Adab of hand use in wudu with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using right hand for rinsing and sniffing, and left for blowing nose, and identify the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Right hand for honored actions, left for unpleasant ones—a sunnah of wudu, not an obligation.

This lesson covers a beautiful adab (etiquette) of wudu: using the right hand for rinsing the mouth and sniffing water, and the left hand for blowing the nose. While these actions are part of the recommended sunan, the underlying principle—using the right for good and left for what is unpleasant—reflects the prophetic guidance in daily acts of purity. We will examine the proofs and understand why this is not a strict duty but a meritorious practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that rinsing (madmadah) and sniffing (istinshaq) should be done with the right hand, and blowing the nose (imtikhat) with the left. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or adab?
The passage calls it 'adab' (protocol/etiquette). In Hanafi fiqh, this is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: a hadith from Aisha (RA) describing the Prophet's practice, and another from Humran witnessing Uthman (RA) performing wudu. Identify which hadith provides the general principle and which gives a specific example.
The first hadith is general, the second is specific and directly shows using the right hand for rinsing and sniffing.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith prove the ruling. For Aisha's hadith, the Prophet used his right hand for pure actions (tahur, food) and left for impure ones. Rinsing and sniffing are pure, so right hand. For Uthman's hadith, it explicitly shows him using his right hand for these acts. This provides evidence for the recommended nature.
The evidence is zanni in transmission and indication, so it establishes a mustahabb ruling, not wajib.
4
Note the epistemological weight
Assess the authority of this ruling. It comes from Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon across madhhabs (muttafaq alayh). There is no intra-Hanafi dispute. The mufta bihi is to follow this adab.
Although the proofs are ahad, the ruling is widely accepted and not contested.

Source Text

(۱۱۰) والمضمضة والاستنشاق باليد اليمنى والامتخاط باليسرى

ترجمه : (۱۱۰) [۱۰] مضمضہ اور استنشاق دائیں ہاتھ سے کرنا۔ [11] ناک بائیں ہاتھ سے صاف کرنا۔

تشریح: کلی کرنا ہو یا ناک میں پانی ڈالنا ہو تو دائیں ہاتھ سے کرے، اور پھر صاف کرنا ہو تو بائیں ہاتھ سے کرے، یہ ادب ہے وجه : کلی کرنا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا محترم چیز ہے اس لئے اس کو دائیں ہاتھ سے کرے،اور ناک صاف کرنا نا پسندیدہ چیز ہے اس لئے اس کو بائیں ہاتھ سے انجام دے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے (۲) ۔ عن عائشة قالت كانت يد رسول الله اليمنى لطهوره و طعامه و كانت يده اليسرى لخلائه و ما كان من اذى ابوداود شریف، باب کراھیة مس الذکر باليمين في الاستبراء، ص ۱۷، نمبر ۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ اچھے کام کے لئے اور بائیں ہاتھ نا پسندیدہ کام کے لئے استعمال ہوتا تھا۔(۳)۔ان حمران مولی عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء ،فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما ، ثم ادخل يمينه فى الاناء فمضمض و استنثر - ( بخاری شریف، باب الوضوء ثلاثا ثلاثا ،ص۳۲ نمبر ۱۵۹ ابوداود شریف ، باب صفته وضوء النبی ص ص ۲۶، نمبر (۱۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ سے مضمضہ اور استنشاق کیا۔ لغت : امتخاط: مخط سے مشتق ہے، بچے کی ناک سے رینٹ صاف کرنا۔ یسری: بائیں ہاتھ
(110) And rinsing the mouth and sniffing water with the right hand, and blowing the nose with the left. Translation: (110) [10] To rinse the mouth and to take water into the nose with the right hand. [11] To clean the nose with the left hand. Explanation: Whether it is rinsing the mouth or putting water into the nose, one should do it with the right hand. Then when cleaning (blowing) the nose, do it with the left hand. This is a protocol (adab) because rinsing the mouth and putting water into the nose are honored actions, so they should be done with the right hand, while cleaning the nose is a disliked action, so it should be done with the left hand. (2) There is a hadith: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The right hand of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was for his purification and his food, and his left hand was for his toilet and what was harmful. (Abu Dawud, chapter on dislike of touching the penis with the right hand during istibra', p. 17, no. 33) This hadith indicates that the right hand was used for good things and the left for disliked things. (3) And from Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, that he informed him that he saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, then he poured water over his hands three times and washed them, then he put his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and blew his nose. (Bukhari, chapter on three-three wudu, p. 32, no. 159; Abu Dawud, chapter on description of the Prophet's wudu, p. 26, no. 108) This hadith shows that he rinsed and sniffed with the right hand. Lexicon: امتخاط (imtikhat) is derived from makhit, meaning to clean mucus from a child's nose. یسری (yusra) means left hand.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage explains the etiquettes of wudu concerning the use of hands. It is a recommended practice (adab) to use the right hand for rinsing the mouth and putting water into the nose, and to use the left hand for blowing the nose. The reasoning is that the right hand should be used for honored actions and the left for unpleasant ones. The author provides two proofs from hadith: first, a general hadith from Aisha describing the Prophet's practice of using his right hand for purity and food and his left for toiletry; second, a specific practice of Uthman ibn Affan who used his right hand for rinsing and sniffing. This establishes the recommended nature of these actions in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): rinsing the mouth with water
استنشاق (istinshaq): drawing water into the nose
امتخاط (imtikhat): blowing the nose to expel mucus
يمين (yamin): right hand
يسار (yasar): left hand

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm level of using the right hand for rinsing the mouth (madmadah) during wudu in the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb (adab)
D) Makruh tahrimi

Key Takeaway
Using the right hand for rinsing and sniffing, and the left for blowing the nose, is a recommended sunnah (mustahabb) based on prophetic practice, not an obligation.

Performing Wudu Before the Time of Prayer
Ruling on performing wudu before prayer time for one without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on performing wudu before prayer time for a person without excuse and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Performing wudu before prayer time is mustahabb, not obligatory, and indicates faith.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on performing wudu before the designated prayer time. The text clarifies this is a recommended act (mustahabb) for those who have no valid excuse. We will also look at the hadith evidence that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu before the prayer time for one without an excuse. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
Note the condition 'without an excuse' — this is key.
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites a hadith from Thawban: 'None guards purification except a believer.' This is the dalil for the ruling.
Hadith source: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove it is mustahabb? The hadith praises those who maintain purification, implying that early wudu is a virtuous act of faith.
The praise without command indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the condition of 'udhr
The ruling is specifically for those without a valid excuse. If there is an excuse, the recommendation may be lifted or delayed.
This reflects the Hanafi attention to individual circumstances.

(۱۱۱) والتوضأ قبل دخول الوقت لغير المعذور

ترجمه : (۱۱) [۱۲] اگر عذر نہ ہو تو وقت سے پہلے وضو کر لینا۔

تشریح : وقت سے پہلے وضو کر نا نماز کی اہمیت کا پتہ دیتا ہے اس لئے اگر عذر نہ ہو تو نماز کے وقت سے پہلے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے وجه : عن ثوبان مولى رسول الله الله قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يحافظ على الطهور الا مؤمن ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی المحافظة على الوضوء وفضله ، ج اول ص ۱۴، نمبر ۳۵) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ وقت سے پہلے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے۔
(111) And performing wudu before the entry of the time for one who has no excuse. Translation: (11) [12] If there is no excuse, to perform wudu before the time. Explanation: Performing wudu before the time indicates the importance of prayer. Therefore, if one has no excuse, performing wudu before the prayer time is mustahabb. Proof: From Thawban, the freed slave of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, none guards the purification except a believer.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on guarding wudu and its virtue, vol. 1, p. 14, no. 35) This hadith indicates that performing wudu before the time is mustahabb.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This ruling addresses the recommendation to perform wudu before the prayer time when one has no valid excuse. The author states that doing so shows the importance of prayer and is therefore mustahabb (recommended). The proof is a hadith from Thawban reporting the Prophet's statement that only a believer guards purification. The implication is that performing wudu in advance is a sign of faith. In the Hanafi school, this is considered a recommended practice, not obligatory. However, if one has an excuse (such as difficulty in maintaining wudu), it may be preferable to delay.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): a valid excuse that prevents performing wudu at the usual time
مستحب (mustahabb): recommended, not obligatory; doing it earns reward, leaving it is not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a sign of faith.
B) It is obligatory.
C) It is a means to avoid sin.
D) It is a condition for prayer.

Key Takeaway
Performing wudu before prayer time is mustahabb for those without excuse, as it demonstrates eagerness for prayer and is a sign of faith.

Reciting the Shahada After Wudu: A Recommended Act with Great Reward
Ruling with proof for a recommended act after wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (mustahabb) on reciting the shahada after wudu and identify the hadith proof and its implications.

Core Idea
Reciting the shahada after wudu is mustahabb, not wajib; the hadith promises eight gates of paradise.

After completing wudu, many Muslims recite the testimony of faith. This lesson explores the ruling on this act, clarifying that it is a recommended sunnah (mustahabb), not an obligation. Understanding this distinction helps you avoid confusing mustahabb with wajib and appreciate the immense reward promised for this simple act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is reciting the shahada (the two testimonies) after wudu. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
Mustahabb means the act is meritorious but omission does not invalidate wudu.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik (ra) recorded by Ibn Majah (no. 469). The hadith explicitly promises reward for this act.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator chain), so it yields zanni (speculative) certainty in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication of meaning)
The explicit promise of opening the eight gates of paradise indicates that the act is highly recommended and meritorious. This is the basis for the Hanafi ruling of mustahabb.
A promise of reward typically indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (difference of opinion)
There is no significant intra- or inter-madhhab dispute; most schools agree on its recommendation.
The Hanafi position is the same as the majority.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (operative ruling)
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that reciting the shahada after wudu is mustahabb. It is a sunnah practice with great reward.
It is not part of the wajibat of wudu; omitting it does not affect the validity of wudu.

Source Text

(۱۱۲) والاتيان بالشهادتين بعد الوضوء

ترجمه : (۱۱۲) [۱۳] وضو کے بعد کلمہ شہادت پڑھنا۔

وجه : اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک عن النبى الله الله قال من توضأ فاحسن الوضوء ثم قال ثلاث مرات اشهد ان لا اله الا الله وحده لا شريك له و اشهد ان محمدا عبده و رسوله فتح له ثمانية ابواب الجنة من أيها شاء دخل (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما یقال بعد الوضوء ، ص ۶۷ نمبر ۴۶۹ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کے بعد شہادتین پڑھے۔
(112) And reciting the two testimonies after wudu. Translation: (112) [13] To recite the kalima shahada after wudu. Proof: There is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'Whoever performs wudu and does it well, then says three times: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger, the eight gates of paradise will be opened for him, and he may enter through whichever he wishes.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on what is said after wudu, p. 67, no. 469) This hadith indicates that one should recite the shahada after wudu.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This lesson presents a recommended practice (mustahabb) after completing wudu: to recite the shahada (testimony of faith) three times. The proof is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik, where the Prophet promises that doing so will cause the eight gates of paradise to be opened for the person, allowing entry through any gate. This highlights the immense reward for this simple act. In the Hanafi school, reciting the shahada after wudu is considered a sunnah or mustahabb, based on this hadith. The text also mentions that the shahada should be recited three times, although some versions mention once. The practice of reciting it three times is followed based on this narration.

Key Terms
شهادتين (shahadatayn): the two testimonies: 'La ilaha illallah' and 'Muhammadun Rasulullah'
توضأ فاحسن الوضوء (tawadda'a fa ahsana al-wudu): performed wudu and did it well, i.e., performed it properly according to the sunnah

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Three times

D) As many times as one wishes

Key Takeaway
Reciting the shahada after wudu is a mustahabb act with great reward (eight gates of paradise), not a condition for the validity of wudu.

Drinking Leftover Wudu Water and Supplication
A matn ruling with proof from the practice of Ali and the Prophet's Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for drinking leftover wudu water while standing and for the post-wudu supplication, and identify their proofs.

Core Idea
Drinking leftover wudu water standing and reciting the repentant's supplication are recommended acts rooted in the practice of the Prophet and his Companions.

Wudu leaves behind blessed water. The Hanafi school recommends drinking this leftover water while standing and reciting a beautiful supplication. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the practice of Ali and the Prophet's own action with Zamzam, showing that these acts are mustahabb (recommended) and carry spiritual benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their ruling
The passage presents two separate recommended acts: drinking leftover wudu water while standing, and reciting a specific supplication after wudu. Both are classified as mustahabb in the Hanafi school.
Mustahabb means recommended, not obligatory. Doing them earns reward; leaving them is not sinful.
2
Locate the first proof for drinking standing
The author cites the athar from Abu Hayyah who saw Ali perform the Prophet's wudu and then drink the leftover water standing. This shows the practice of a companion directly emulating the Prophet.
Ali explicitly said he intended to show the Prophet's purification, making this a strong proof.
3
Analyze the additional analogy to Zamzam
The author further compares leftover wudu water to Zamzam water, which the Prophet drank standing. This strengthens the recommendation by drawing an analogy (qiyas) between two blessed waters.
The proof for Zamzam is from Ibn Abbas's hadith in Bukhari.
4
Find the proof for the supplication
The supplication is proven by another athar of Ali: after finishing wudu, he would recite the shahada and then ask Allah to make him among the repentant and purified.
This shows the supplication is a sunna derived from a companion's practice, which is acceptable in Hanafi usul.
5
Conclude the ruling and its scope
Both acts are mustahabb, not wajib. They are rooted in authentic practices and are recommended for all Muslims after wudu.
There is no known dispute among schools; all consider these acts recommended.

(۱۱۳) وان يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائما وان يقول اللهم اجعلنى من التوابين و اجعلني من المتطهرين.

ترجمه : (۱۱۳) [۱۴] کھڑے ہو کر وضو سے بچے ہوئے پانی کو پینا اور یہ دعا پڑھنا:’ الـلـهـم اجـعـلـنـى من التوابين واجعلني من المتطهرين ، یعنی اے اللہ ! مجھ کو توبہ کرنے والوں میں سے کیجئے اور پاک لوگوں میں کر دیجئے۔

وجه : کھڑا ہو کر وضو کا بچا ہوا پانی پینا مستحب ہے اس کا ثبوت اس اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابى حية قال رأيت عليا توضأ فأنقى كفيه ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و ذراعيه ثلاثا و مسح برأسه ثم غسل قدميه الى الكعبين ثم قام فشرب فضل وضوئه ثم قال انما اردت ان أريكم طهور رسول الله لا ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی الوضوء كم مرة ، ج اول، ص ۱۶، نمبر ۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کا بچا ہوا پانی کھڑا ہو کر پیئے ۔ (۲) یہ ماء زمزم کی طرح اہم پانی ہے اس لئے اس کو بھی کھڑا ہو کر پینا چاہئے ، ماء زمزم کھڑا ہو کر پینے کا ثبوت یہ ہے۔ ان ابن عباس حـدثـه قـال سـقـيـت رسول الله له من زمزم فشرب وهو قائم - ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما جاء فی زمزم، ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۶۳۷) (۳) اور دعا پڑھنے کا ثبوت اس عمل صحابی میں ہے۔ كـان عـلى اذا فـرغ من وضـوئه قـال اشـهـد ان لا اله الا الله وحـده لا شـریـك له و اشـهـد ان مـحـمـدا عـبـده و رسـوله، رب اجعلني من التوابین و اجعلنى من المتطهرين - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما يقول اذا فرغ من وضـوه ، ج اول ص ۱۳، نمبر ۲۰) اس حدیث میں یہ دعاء ہے۔
(113) And that he drink from the leftover wudu water while standing, and that he say: 'O Allah, make me among the repentant and make me among the purified.' Translation: (113) [14] To drink the leftover water from wudu while standing, and to recite this supplication: 'O Allah, make me among the repentant and make me among the purified.' Proof: Drinking the leftover wudu water while standing is mustahabb. Its proof is this athar: From Abu Hayyah who said: I saw Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) perform wudu: he cleaned his palms, then washed his face three times, his forearms three times, wiped his head, then washed his feet up to the ankles, then he stood up and drank the leftover water of his wudu, then said: 'I only wanted to show you the purification of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on how many times in wudu, vol. 1, p. 16, no. 54) This hadith indicates that one should drink the leftover wudu water standing. (2) This water is important like Zamzam water, therefore it should also be drunk standing. The proof for drinking Zamzam water standing is that Ibn Abbas narrated: 'I gave the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from Zamzam, and he drank while standing.' (Bukhari, chapter on Zamzam, p. 265, no. 1637) (3) And the proof for reciting the supplication is the practice of a companion: Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when he finished his wudu used to say: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. O Lord, make me among the repentant and make me among the purified.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on what to say when finished wudu, vol. 1, p. 13, no. 20) This hadith contains this supplication.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents two recommended acts after wudu: drinking the leftover water while standing, and reciting a specific supplication. The author proves the first by the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib, who demonstrated the Prophet's wudu and then drank the leftover water standing. Additionally, the author compares the water to Zamzam, which is also drunk standing as per the Prophet's practice. The supplication is proven by Ali's own practice of reciting the shahada and then asking Allah to make him among the repentant and purified. In the Hanafi school, both acts are considered mustahabb (recommended). The standing posture for drinking the leftover water is not obligatory but preferred due to the emulation of the Prophet and the companions.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudu): the leftover water that remains in the vessel after performing wudu
قائما (qa'iman): in a standing posture
توابین (tawwabin): those who frequently repent
متطهرین (mutatahhirin): those who are purified (physically and spiritually)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He wiped his neck
B) He drank the leftover water standing
C) He sat down and prayed
D) He poured the water away

Key Takeaway
Drinking leftover wudu water while standing and reciting the du'a are recommended acts, proven by the practice of Ali and the Prophet's Sunnah with Zamzam.

Recommended Acts After Wudu: Shahadah and Drinking Leftover Water
Explains recommended acts after wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two recommended acts after wudu, identify their evidence from hadith and companion practice, and explain why they are mustahabb rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Reciting shahadah and drinking leftover wudu water are mustahabb acts that increase reward, not obligations.

In this passage, the author outlines two courteous acts (adab) after completing wudu. These actions are not required for the validity of wudu but are highly encouraged. We will examine the textual evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Companions' example, and understand the Hanafi classification of these acts as mustahabb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The text lists two actions: reciting the shahadah three times after wudu, and drinking the leftover wudu water while standing while reciting a specific dua ('Allahumma aj'alni min al-tawwabeen...').
2
Examine the first proof
For the shahadah, the author cites a hadith from Anas ibn Malik (Ibn Majah): whoever performs wudu well and says the shahadah thrice will have all eight gates of Paradise opened. The mention of reward indicates istihbab, not obligation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it cannot establish wujub.
3
Examine the second proof
For drinking leftover water, the author presents an athar from Abu Hayyah reporting that Ali (RA) performed wudu, then drank the leftover water standing, saying he wanted to show the Prophet's practice. The author also analogizes to drinking Zamzam water standing, as the Prophet did.
The athar from Ali and the analogy to Zamzam strengthen the recommendation.
4
Determine the ruling level
All these acts are classified as mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah). They are rewarded but not obligatory; omitting them does not incur sin. The evidence is zanni and does not reach the level of wujub.
Hanafi usul: a command with reward but no threat of punishment indicates istihbab.

Six Disliked Acts in Wudu (Makruhat al-Wudu)
Lists six makruhat in wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six disliked acts in wudu according to the Hanafi school and identify the textual evidence for each.

Core Idea
Extravagance and stinginess in wudu are both disliked; the Prophet’s way is moderation.

Wudu is an act of worship with etiquettes and boundaries. While we often focus on what is obligatory, the Hanafi school also highlights six actions that are makruh (disliked). These include extremes in water use, forceful washing, worldly talk, unnecessary help, and repeated wiping with fresh water. This lesson presents each with its proof from hadith or athar, helping you refine your practice.

Guided Path
1
List the six disliked acts
Read the passage and enumerate each makruh exactly as described. Note that the first two (israf and taqtir) are often paired.
The acts are: 1) Israf, 2) Taqtir, 3) Latm, 4) Worldly talk, 5) Seeking help without excuse, 6) Repeating masah with new water.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For each makruh, find the specific hadith or athar cited. Identify whether the proof is a direct statement of the Prophet or a companion practice.
E.g., for israf/taqtir, the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the hadith 'whoever adds or subtracts has done wrong' are used.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates dislike. For israf: the Prophet's moderate usage; for taqtir: the warning of 'asaa wa zalam'.
The key is that the Prophet's practice and explicit condemnation establish the ruling.
4
Note cross-madhhab differences
Recognize that some schools may not consider all six as makruh. For example, speaking during wudu is allowed in other schools.
This difference arises from whether wudu is seen as a purely physical act or a ritual requiring mindfulness.
5
Apply to your own practice
Reflect on common habits: Do you use too much water? Do you avoid talking? The goal is to follow the prophetic moderation.
Being mindful of these disliked acts increases the reward and perfection of wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : ويكره للمتوضى ستة اشياء . (١١٤) الاسراف في الماء والتقتير فيه . فصل في مكروهات الوضوء ترجمه : (١١٤) وضو کرنے والے کے لئے چھ چیزیں مکروہ ہیں : [1] پانی زیادہ خرچ کرنا ، [۲] اور بہت کم خرچ کرنا۔ تشریح : وضو کے لئے جتنا پانی مناسب ہے اس سے بہت زیادہ استعمال کرنا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس میں پانی کا اسراف ہے اور جتنا مناسب ہے اس سے بہت کم خرچ کرنا بھی مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ کوئی عضو سوکھا رہ جائے ، تین تین مرتبہ نہ دھو سکے جو سنت ہے . وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ ان ابن عباس بات ليلة عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فقام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الى القربة فسكب منها فتوضأ و لم يكثر من الماء و لم يقصر فى الوضوء ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تین تین مرتبہ سے زیادہ دھونا بھی ظلم ہے، برا ہے، اور کم کرنا بھی ظلم ہے اور برا ہے، اس لئے دونوں مکروہ ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده قال ان رجلا اتى النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله ! كيف الطهور ؟ فدعا بماء في اناء فغسل كفيه ثلاثا ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا ثم غسل ذراعيه ثلاثا ثم مسح برأسه و ادخل اصبعيه السباحتين في اذنيه و مسح بابهاميه على ظاهر اذنيه و بالسباحتين باطن اذنيه ثم غسل رجليه ثلاثا ثلاثا ثم قال هكذا الوضوء ، فمن زاد على هذا او نقص فقد اساء و ظلم او ظلم و أساء . (۳) عن هلال بن يساف قال كان يقال في الوضوء اسراف و لو كان على شاطى نهر . لغت : اسراف : حد سے زیادہ خرچ کرنا۔ تفسير : قتر سے مشتق ہے، کمی کرنا۔ ترجمه : (١١٥) [۳] چہرے پر زور سے پانی مارنا۔ [ مکروہ ہے] وجه : (1) عن ابن عباس قال دخل على علی یعنی ابی طالب و قد اهرق الماء ..... ثم أخذ بكفه اليمنى قبضة من ماء فصبها على ناصيته فتركها تستن علی وجهه (۲) سمع جابر بن عبد الله يقول نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الوسم في الوجه و الضرب فى الوجه (۳) عن ابراهيم قال كانوا يكرهون ان يلطموا وجوههم بالماء لطما و كانوا يمسحونها قليلا قليلا۔ ترجمه : (١١٦) [۴] وضو میں دنیوی باتیں کرنا۔ تشریح : وضو عبادت ہے اس لئے اس میں دعا پڑھنی چاہئے اس لئے دنیوی باتیں کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ ترجمه : (١١٧) (۵) بغیر عذر دوسرے سے مدد لینا ۔ [ مکروہ ہے] تشریح : عذر ہو تو دوسروں سے مدد لینا جائز ہے، اس کے لئے حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ وجه : عن العباس بن عبد الرحمن المدنى قال خصلتان لم يكن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يكلهما الى احد من اهله كان يناول المسكين بيده و يضع الطهور من الليل و يخمره۔ ترجمه : (١١٨) [ ۶ ] نئے پانی سے تین بار مسح کرنا۔ تشریح : ایک ہی پانی سے تین بار سر کا مسح کرے یہ تو جائز ہے لیکن تین مرتبہ الگ الگ پانی لے اور تین بار سر کا مسح کرے یہ اسراف ہے اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔
Chapter: Six things are disliked for the one performing wudu. (114) Extravagance in water and stinginess in it. Translation: (114) Six things are disliked for the one performing wudu: [1] Using too much water, [2] using too little water. Explanation: Using much more water than is appropriate for wudu is disliked because it is wasteful, and using much less than appropriate is also disliked because it may result in a limb remaining dry and not being able to wash three times, which is Sunnah. Evidence: (1) This hadith: Ibn Abbas spent the night at the Prophet's house and saw him take water from a skin and perform wudu without using too much or too little water. (2) This hadith: Washing more than three times is oppression and wrongdoing, and less is also oppression and wrongdoing, so both are disliked. The Prophet said: 'This is wudu; whoever adds or subtracts has done wrong and oppressed.' (3) The narration: It was said that in wudu there is extravagance even if one is on the bank of a river. Lexicon: israf means spending beyond the limit; taqtir means stinginess. Translation: (115) [3] Striking the face forcefully with water. [disliked] Evidence: (1) Ibn Abbas said that Ali poured water on his forehead and let it flow over his face. (2) Jabir reported that the Prophet forbade striking the face. (3) Ibrahim said they disliked slapping the face with water and would wipe gently. Translation: (116) [4] Speaking worldly talk during wudu. Explanation: Wudu is worship, so one should recite supplications; therefore worldly talk is disliked. Translation: (117) (5) Seeking help from others without excuse. [disliked] Explanation: If there is an excuse, seeking help is permissible; a hadith has passed on this. Evidence: The Prophet himself would bring the water for wudu and cover it. Translation: (118) [6] Repeating the masah (wiping) of the head three times with new water. Explanation: Wiping the head three times with the same water is permissible, but taking new water each time is wasteful and therefore disliked.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section enumerating the six disliked acts (makruhat) in wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author first lists them then provides evidence from hadith and athar. The first two are extravagance (israf) and stinginess (taqtir) in water usage; the proof includes the Prophet's practice of moderation and the warning that excess or deficiency is injustice. The third is striking the face with water forcefully, as the Prophet gently poured water instead. The fourth is engaging in worldly conversation, because wudu is an act of worship deserving of dhikr. The fifth is seeking assistance without a valid excuse, as the Prophet preferred to do his own wudu. The sixth is wiping the head three times with fresh water each time, which is wasteful; using the same water is sufficient. All rulings are based on explicit textual evidence (hadith and athar) and are classified as makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اسراف (israf): Excessive use of water beyond what is needed for valid wudu.
تقتير (taqtir): Using too little water such that a limb may remain dry or the Sunnah of three washes is not fulfilled.
لطم (latm): Striking or slapping the face with water forcefully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Striking the face with water forcefully
D) Seeking help without excuse

Key Takeaway
Moderation in wudu is the prophetic way; both excess and deficiency are disliked.

Disliked Acts in Wudu: Rulings and Their Proofs
Listing four disliked acts in wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four disliked acts in wudu according to the Hanafi school, cite the proofs for each, and explain why they are considered makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Four acts in wudu are makruh tanzihi due to waste (israf) or deviation from prophetic practice.

Wudu is a sacred act of worship, and following the Sunnah enhances its reward. However, certain actions, though not invalidating wudu, are disliked because they contradict the prophetic method or involve waste. This lesson examines four such acts, each supported by explicit hadith evidence, and clarifies their ruling according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the four disliked acts
From the text, list the four acts: (1) striking the face with water forcefully, (2) speaking worldly talk, (3) seeking help from another without excuse, (4) wiping the head three times with fresh water each time.
The text numbers them as 115-118.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For each act, identify the specific proof cited: hadith from Ibn Abbas for striking, narration from Ibrahim for striking, hadith from Abbas for self-reliance, and hadith from Amr ibn Shuayb for triple wipe.
The proofs are from Abu Dawud, Musnad Ahmad, and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates dislike. For striking: the Prophet let water flow; striking contradicts that. For worldly talk: wudu is worship; talk distracts. For seeking help: the Prophet did it himself. For triple wipe: the hadith says 'whoever adds or subtracts has done wrong', indicating wastage.
The underlying principle is israf (waste) and following Sunnah.
4
Note exceptions and conditions
Seeking help is permissible with a valid excuse (illness, old age). Triple wipe with the same water is not disliked; only with fresh water each time.
This is from the text's explanation.
5
Apply the Hanafi classification of makruh tanzihi
These acts are makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) because the proofs are ahad hadith and the prohibition is not absolute. Avoiding them is rewarded, but doing them does not incur sin.
Compare with makruh tahrimi which is closer to haram.

(مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يحب ان یلی طهوره بنفسه ، ج اول ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۲۰۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور خود وضو کا پانی لاتے۔ ترجمه : (۱۱۸) [ ۶ ] نئے پانی سے تین بار مسح کرنا۔ تشریح : ایک ہی پانی سے تین بار سر کا مسح کرے یہ تو جائز ہے لیکن تین مرتبہ الگ الگ پانی لے اور تین بار سر کا مسح کرے یہ اسراف ہے اس لئے یہ مکروہ ہے۔ عـن عـمـر و بـن شـعـيــب عـن ابــه عــن جــده قــال ان رجلا اتــى النبي صلى الله ..... ثم مسح برأ برأسه و ادخل اصبعيه السباحتين في اذنيه و مسـح بـابـهـاميه على ظاهر اذنيه و بالسباحتيـن بـاطـن اذنيه ثم غسل رجليه ثلاثا ثلاثا ثم قال هكذا الوضوء ، فمن زاد على هذا او نقص فقد اساء و ظلم او ظلم و أساء - ابوداود شریف، باب الوضوء ثلاثا ص ۲۹ نمبر ۱۳۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اس سے زیادہ کرے تو ظلم کیا اور کم کرے تب بھی ظلم ہے۔
Section on disliked acts of wudu: (115) Striking the face with water; (116) Speaking worldly talk; (117) Seeking help from another without excuse; (118) Wiping the head three times with new water. ... Translation: (115) [3] Striking the face forcefully with water [is disliked]. Evidence: ... (116) [4] Speaking worldly talk during wudu. Explanation: Wudu is worship, so one should recite supplications; therefore worldly talk is disliked. (117) (5) Seeking help from another without excuse [is disliked]. Explanation: If there is an excuse, it is permissible; the hadith has passed. (118) [6] Wiping three times with new water. Explanation: Wiping the head three times with the same water is permissible, but taking fresh water each time is wasteful, hence disliked.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage lists four disliked acts (makruhat) in wudu, each supported by explicit textual evidence. First, striking the face forcefully with water (item 115) is proven by a hadith from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet's practice of letting water flow, and by the prohibition of striking the face. Second, speaking worldly talk (116) is disliked because wudu is an act of worship; one should instead recite supplications. Third, seeking help from another without a valid excuse (117) is disliked, as the Prophet himself would prepare his own wudu water. However, if one has an excuse (e.g., illness), it is permissible. Fourth, wiping the head three times with fresh water each time (118) is disliked due to waste (israf), while wiping thrice with the same water is permissible. The hadith of 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb teaches that the sunnah wudu is one wipe of the head; exceeding that is oppression (zulm). Thus, the Hanafi school considers these acts makruh tanzihan (lightly disliked).

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An act that is disliked but not sinful; avoiding it is rewarded but doing it is not punished.
اسراف (israf): Wasting resources beyond need; here specifically using more water than necessary in wudu.
مسح (masah): Wiping a part of the body with wet hands; in wudu, wiping the head is an integral act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a disliked act (makruh) in wudu?
A) Wiping the head once with the same water
B) Striking the face forcefully with water
C) Reciting supplications during wudu
D) Using leftover water from a previous wudu

Key Takeaway
Four acts are makruh tanzihi in wudu: striking face, worldly talk, seeking help without excuse, and triple wipe with fresh water; avoiding them follows the Sunnah.

The Three Categories of Wudu in the Hanafi School
Dividing wudu into three categories based on obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fard, wajib, and mustahab categories of wudu and state the ruling for each based on the action to be performed.

Core Idea
Wudu is fard for acts that require purity, wajib for acts that become makruh without it, and mustahab otherwise.

In the Hanafi school, wudu is not always obligatory to the same degree. Its ruling depends on the action you intend to perform. This lesson classifies wudu into three categories: fard (obligatory from definitive evidence), wajib (necessary from probable evidence), and mustahab (recommended). Understanding these categories ensures you know when wudu is essential for validity, when it is necessary to avoid sin, and when it is simply rewarding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act you intend to perform
Consider the specific action you wish to do, such as salah, tawaf, or reciting Qur'an without touching.
2
Determine if the act is valid without wudu
If the act is invalid without wudu (e.g., any salah regardless of fard/nafl), then wudu is fard. If it is valid but makruh without wudu (e.g., tawaf), then wudu is wajib. If it is valid and not makruh without wudu (e.g., renewing wudu), then wudu is mustahab.
The text lists four actions for which wudu is fard: general salah, janazah salah, sajdah tilawah, and touching the Qur'an.
3
Apply the category
Match the act to one of the three categories: fard, wajib, or mustahab. This determines the legal obligation to perform wudu.
The Hanafi school distinguishes fard (based on qat'i evidence) from wajib (based on zanni evidence), though both are obligatory in practice.

( ترندی شریف باب ما جاء لا تقبل صلوۃ بغیر طھور ، ص ۱ نمبر 1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ، اسی طرح جو چیزیں نماز کے درجے
Section on categories of wudu: (119) First: It is fard upon the one in a state of minor impurity for salah, even if nafl, and for janazah salah, sajdah tilawah, and touching the Qur'an. ... Explanation: Here he mentions four actions for which wudu is fard: general salah (even nafl), janazah salah (if time permits, tayammum may be used), sajdah tilawah, and touching the Qur'an (even a verse). Evidence: Hadith from Ibn Umar: 'Salah is not accepted without purification, and charity is not accepted from ill-gotten gains.'
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage defines the three categories of wudu based on the ruling of the action it precedes. First, wudu is fard (obligatory) for actions that cannot be valid without it: regular salah (including nafl), janazah salah, sajdah tilawah, and touching the Qur'an. The proof is the hadith 'No salah is accepted without purification.' Second, wudu is wajib (necessary) for actions that are valid without it but become makruh if performed without wudu, such as tawaf. Third, wudu is mustahab (recommended) for actions that are valid and not makruh without it, such as renewing wudu or wudu for adhan. The author notes 28 instances where wudu is mustahab. The Hanafi classification distinguishes between fard (based on definitive evidence) and wajib (based on probable evidence); here, the term 'fard' is used for the first category following the madhhab's terminology.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligation established by definitive evidence; omitting it incurs sin.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by probable evidence; omitting it is sinful but slightly less severe than fard.
مستحب (mustahab): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah tilawah): The prostration (sajdah) performed when reciting specific verses of the Qur'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of wudu for performing nafl (voluntary) salah?
A) Mustahab (recommended)
B) Wajib (necessary)
C) Fard (obligatory)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
The ruling of wudu depends on the act: fard if the act requires purity, wajib if the act is valid but makruh without it, and mustahab otherwise.

Wudu is Fard for Salah, Janazah, Tilawah, and Touching Quran
States the first category of wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four acts for which wudu is fard and identify the Hanafi evidence for each act.

Core Idea
Wudu is fard for any prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, and touching the Quran.

In this passage, the author introduces the Hanafi classification of wudu into three categories. The first and most important category is when wudu becomes fard (obligatory). Four specific acts require wudu before performance; without wudu, these acts are invalid. The passage then provides the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that wudu is 'fard' for a person in hadath for four acts. Understand that 'fard' here means the obligation is established by definitive evidence (qati dalil) according to Hanafi usul.
Hanafi school distinguishes fard from wajib; fard is from qati evidence.
2
List the four acts
The four acts are: (1) any prayer, including nafl; (2) funeral prayer (salat al-janazah); (3) the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah); (4) touching the Quran, even a single verse.
Note that the author explicitly includes nafl prayers and even a single verse of Quran.
3
Analyze the proof for prayer
The hadith 'لا تقبل صلوة بغير طهور' (Prayer is not accepted without purification) is the primary proof. This is a marfu hadith from Ibn Umar. The negation indicates that prayer without wudu is invalid. By qiyas, funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah are included as they resemble prayer.
The hadith is classed as ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear.
4
Analyze the proof for touching Quran
The Quranic verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون' (None touch it except the purified) (56:79) directly proves that touching the Quran requires taharah. This is a qati dalil (Quran) for the obligation.
Some schools interpret this as referring to angels, but Hanafi takes the apparent meaning.
5
Examine the companion statement
The athar of Ibn Umar explicitly states that a man should not prostrate (for tilawah) or pray over the janazah unless he is pure. This provides additional evidence for the obligation on those two acts.
Qawl al-sahabi is considered a proof in Hanafi usul when it does not contradict qiyas.

ضروری نوٹ : یہاں وضو کی تین قسمیں بیان کی ہیں [1] جس کے لئے وضو کرنا فرض ہو [۲] وضوکرنا واجب ہو [۳] وضوکرنا مستحب ہو ۔ [1] ایسا کام جو وضو کے بغیر ہو ہی نہیں سکتا ہو جیسے نماز پڑھنا، نماز جنازہ پڑھنا وضو کے بغیر ہو ہی نہیں سکتا، اس کے لئے وضو کر نا فرض ہے ۔ [۲] اور جو کام وضو کے بغیر ہو تو سکتا ہو لیکن مکروہ ہو ، جیسے طواف کعبہ بغیر وضو کے ہوسکتا ہے لیکن مکروہ ہے تو اس کے لئے وضو کرنا واجب ہے ۔ [۳] اور جو کام بغیر وضو کے درست ہو ، جیسے وضو پر وضو کرنا ، یا اذان کے لئے وضو کرنا تو یہ وضو مستحب ہے ،مصنف نے اس کے لئے ۲۸ نام گنائے ہیں ۔ اس طرح وضو کی تین قسمیں ہوگئیں۔
وضو کی تین قسمیں ہیں: ترجمه : (۱۱۹) پہلی قسم : بے وضو والے پر نماز کے لئے وضو کرنا فرض ہے۔ نفل نماز ہو یا نماز جنازہ ہو، یا سجدہ تلاوت ہو اور قرآن مجید کو چھونے کے لئے خواہ ایک آیت ہی ہو۔
تشریح : یہاں وضو فرض ہونے کے لئے چار کام بیان فرما رہے ہیں [1] عام نماز چاہے نفل ہی کیوں نہ ہو بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ہے۔[۲] نماز جنازہ بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ہے، اتنی گنجائش ہے کہ وقت کم ہو تو تیم کرلے[۳] سجدہ تلاوت بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ۔ [۴] قرآن پاک کو چھونا ، چاہے ایک آیت ہی ہو بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں اس لئے ان چاروں کاموں کے لئے وضو کر نا فرض ہے۔
الله
وجه : (ا) عن ابن عمر عن النبي ال الله قال لا تقبل صلوة بغير طهور ، و لا صدقة من غلول - ( ترندی شریف باب ما جاء لا تقبل صلوۃ بغیر طھور ، ص ۱ نمبر 1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ، اسی طرح جو چیزیں نماز کے درجے میں ہیں وہ بھی بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ہوں گی۔ (۲) قرآن کے چھونے کے بارے میں یہ آیت ہے ۔ لا يمسه الا الطهرون ۔ ( آیت ۷۹ ، سورۃ الواقعہ (۵۶) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بغیر یا کی کے قرآن کریم نہ چھوئے ۔ (۳) نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه قال لا يسجد الرجل الا وهو طاهر و لا يقرأ الا وهو طاهر و لا يصلى على الجنازة الا هو طاهر ( سنن بیہقی ، باب استحباب الظهر للذكر والقرآة ، ج اول ص ۱۴۷، نمبر ۴۲۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت بغیر وضو کے نہ کرے۔
Section: The ablution is of three types. Section on the types of ablution. (119) The first is obligatory upon the one in a state of hadath for prayer, even if it is supererogatory, and for the funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation, and for touching the Quran, even one verse. ... Explanation: The author lists four acts for which wudu is obligatory: [1] general prayer even if nafl, [2] funeral prayer, [3] sajdat al-tilawah, [4] touching the Quran. Proof: (1) Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: Prayer is not accepted without purification, nor is charity from ill-gotten gains. (2) For touching the Quran: None touch it except the purified. (3) For funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah: the saying of Ibn Umar that he said: A man should not prostrate unless he is pure, nor recite unless he is pure, nor pray over the deceased unless he is pure.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage opens the topic of the three categories of wudu (ablution) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating a fundamental ruling (matn): wudu is fard (obligatory) for the one in a state of hadath (ritual impurity) for four specific acts: any prayer (fard or nafl), the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration), and touching the Quran (even a single verse). The author then provides three proofs: (1) a hadith from Ibn Umar (marfu) that prayer is not accepted without purification, which includes janazah and tilawah by analogy since they are like prayer; (2) the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (Quran 56:79) establishing that touching the Quran requires taharah; (3) the athar (saying of a companion) of Ibn Umar explicitly prohibiting prostration and janazah prayer without purity. The hanafi position is that these four acts are fard for wudu, meaning the act of wudu itself is fard, not just that the acts are invalid without it. The hadith about wiping the head also appears here as a parenthetical note about the method of wudu, not directly related to this classification.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): An obligation proven by a definitive (qati) evidence; its omission is sinful and requires repetition.
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person who is in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath asghar) requiring wudu.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a prostration command.
لمس القرآن (lams al-Qur'an): Touching the physical copy of the Quran (mushaf) with any part of the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four acts for which wudu is fard according to the passage?
A) Performing the funeral prayer
B) Prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah)
C) Performing tawaf around the Kaaba
D) Touching the Quran

Key Takeaway
Wudu is fard for any valid prayer (including nafl), janazah, sajdat al-tilawah, and touching the Quran, established by hadith, Quran, and companion saying.

Wudu for Tawaf: Wajib, Not Fard
States the second category of wudu: wajib for tawaf with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that wudu is wajib for tawaf in the Hanafi school and explain why it is wajib (not fard), using the hadith evidence and the category of wajib from usul.

Core Idea
Tawaf without wudu is valid but sinful – wajib, not fard.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on wudu for tawaf of the Kaaba. The passage presents three hadith proofs to establish that wudu is wajib (obligatory) but not fard (essential). Understanding this distinction deepens your grasp of the Hanafi hierarchy of legal categories and the role of zanni evidence in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? The passage states that wudu is wajib for tawaf. Note that the ruling is not on tawaf itself but on the requirement of wudu for tawaf.
The author categorizes this as the second type of wudu: wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the evidences cited: three hadith. The first (Ibn Abbas) compares tawaf to salah, except for speech. The second (Aisha) shows that menstruation prevents tawaf until purification. The third (Aisha) records the Prophet's practice of wudu before tawaf.
All are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the requirement of wudu. First: 'mithl al-salah' – analogy for purity requirement. Second: prohibition of tawaf without purification. Third: prophetic action as sunnah and proof of obligation.
The first hadith is the strongest; the word 'mithl' is a clear indicator.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that Shafi'is argue wudu is fard (tawaf invalid without it) based on the same hadith but reading it as indicating fard. Hanafis say wajib because the hadith is zanni, and they rely on the principle that an analogy (tashbih) does not transfer the full ruling.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is compensation vs. invalidity.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۱۳۰)[۲] دوسری قسم : طواف کعبہ کے لئے وضو واجب ہے۔
تشریح یہ وضو کی دوسری قسم ہے۔ کہ کعبہ کے طواف کے لئے وضو واجب ہے، کیونکہ بغیر وضو کے طواف ہو جائے گالیکن مکروہ ہے وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اور نماز میں وضو ضروری ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضوضروری ہوگا۔ اس لئے اگر بغیر وضو کے طواف قدوم کیا تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبى الله قال الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلوة الا انكم تتكلمون فيه فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم الا بخير ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الکلام فی الطواف ص ۱۹۰ حدیث نمبر ۹۶۰ رنسائی شریف ، باب اباحۃ الکلام فی الطواف ج ثانی ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضو شرط ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة انها قالت قدمت مكة وانا حائض ولم اطف بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة قالت فشكوت ذلك الى رسول الله فقال افعلی كما يفعل الحاج غير ان لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تطهری (بخاری شریف، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبیت ص ۲۲۳ نمبر ۱۶۵۰) اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ طہارت کے بغیر طواف نہ کرے ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں طواف کے لئے وضوکا ذکر ہے۔ اخبرتني عائشة ان اول شيء بدأ به حين قدم أنه توضاً ثم طاف بالبيت ثم لم تكن عمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الطاف علی وضوء ، ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۶۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کر کے طواف کیا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے لئے وضو ضروری ہے۔
Translation: (130)[2] The second type: Wudu is obligatory (wajib) for tawaf of the Kaaba. Explanation: This is the second type of wudu. Wudu is wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba because tawaf without wudu is valid but makruh. Proof: (1) The hadith states that tawaf around the House is like prayer except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks should only speak good. This indicates tawaf is like prayer, so wudu is required. (2) Hadith of Aisha: When she was menstruating, the Prophet told her to do all rites of Hajj except tawaf until she purifies. (3) Aisha narrated that the first thing the Prophet did when he arrived (in Mecca) was to perform wudu and then do tawaf.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage discusses the second category of wudu: wudu wajib (obligatory) for tawaf of the Kaaba. The author explains that tawaf performed without wudu is technically valid (the act is done) but is makruh (disliked). Because of this validity, the wudu is not fard but wajib. The evidence includes three hadith: (1) Ibn Abbas reported the Prophet (ﷺ) said 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it.' This analogy (tashbih) establishes that wudu is required for tawaf just as it is for prayer. (2) The hadith of Aisha shows that a menstruating woman cannot perform tawaf until she becomes pure, indicating taharah (purification) is a condition. (3) Aisha's description of the Prophet's actions upon entering Mecca — he performed wudu then tawaf — provides a practical precedent. The Hanafi ruling: wudu is wajib for tawaf, not fard. If one performs tawaf without wudu, it is valid but sinful (makruh tahrimi), and if one is in ihram for Hajj/Umrah, they must perform a dam (sacrifice) as penalty. This is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligation proven by zanni evidence; its omission is sinful but the act is valid if done without it, though with compensation.
الطواف (al-tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times, a rite of Hajj and Umrah.
المكروه (al-makruh): In this context, makruh means makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), as omitting a wajib is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) of wudu for tawaf according to the passage?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Wudu is wajib for tawaf in the Hanafi school: tawaf without it is valid but sinful and requires compensation.
