The Recommended (Mustahabb) Wudu: Sleep and Other Acts
States the third category of wudu: mustahabb, with sleep as an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of mustahabb wudu for sleep and identify at least three other acts for which wudu is mustahabb according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wudu for sleep is mustahabb: performing it earns reward, omitting it incurs no sin.

This lesson examines the third category of wudu in the Hanafi school: mustahabb (recommended). Unlike fard or wajib, mustahabb acts are not obligatory; they are commendable. The passage introduces sleep as a key example and notes that the original compiler listed 28 such acts. We will explore the ruling and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the passage categorizes wudu into three types: fard, wajib, and mustahabb. This lesson focuses on the third type.
The text marks it as (121) والثالث مندوب.
2
Define mustahabb in Hanafi fiqh
Understand that mustahabb (or mandub) is a recommended action: doing it earns reward, leaving it is not sinful. In the Hanafi school, it is often synonymous with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
3
Identify the example of sleep
The passage specifically mentions sleep (للنوم) as one act for which wudu is mustahabb. This is based on the hadith encouraging wudu before sleeping.
The hadith: 'When you go to bed, perform wudu as for prayer.' (Muslim)
4
Note the broader list of 28 acts
The author states that there are 28 such acts. Although the text cuts off, the passage indicates that examples will be given later. Common Hanafi examples include wudu for reciting Quran, entering the mosque, visiting the sick, etc.
The full list is not in this excerpt but is part of the standard Hanafi texts.

ترجمه : (۱۲۱) تیسری قسم : مستحب ہے۔
تشریح : وضو کی تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس کے لئے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے، یعنی کرلے تو اچھا ہے ثواب ملے گا ، اور نہ کرے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ مصنف نے اس کے لئے ۲۸ کام گنائے ہیں ۔ میں ہر ایک کے لئے نمبر ڈال رہا ہوں ۔ ان میں سے بعض کے لئے حدیث مل گئی ہے تو اس کو ذکر کر ہا ہوں، اور بعض مسئلے وہ ہیں جو آگے آرہے ہیں اس کے لئے وہاں حدیث بیان کی جائے گی۔ اور جن
Translation: (121) The third type: Mustahabb (recommended). Explanation: The third type of wudu is that doing wudu for it is mustahabb, meaning if one does it, it is good and he will receive reward, and if he does not do it, there is no harm. The author has enumerated 28 actions for this. I am numbering each one. For some of them a hadith is found, which I will mention, and some issues are those that will come later; for them a hadith will be mentioned there. And those...
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage introduces the third category of wudu: mustahabb (recommended). The author explains that doing wudu for certain acts is commendable but not obligatory; one earns reward for performing it but no sin for leaving it. The author mentions that the original compiler (of the matn) listed 28 such acts. The commentator (the author of Thamaratun Najah) begins to enumerate them with numbers, but the text cuts off mid-sentence, indicating that the full list is continued in later pages. An example of such an act is sleep (as indicated by the matn number 122 'للنوم'). Other common Hanafi examples include: for writing the Quran, for visiting the sick, for entering the mosque, for reading hadith, for dhikr, etc. The Hanafi position: these are mustahabb, not wajib or fard. The source of this recommendation is the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who encouraged wudu in various states.

Key Terms
المستحب (al-mustahabb): An action that is recommended but not obligatory; leaving it is not sinful.
مندوب (al-mandub): Synonym for mustahabb; an action whose performance is loved by Allah but not commanded.
للنوم (lin-nawm): For sleep; a specific act for which wudu is mustahabb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for performing wudu before sleeping according to this passage?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Wudu before sleep and similar acts is mustahabb in the Hanafi school: it is a rewarded Sunnat that carries no sin if omitted.

The Fard Categories of Wudu
Lists the fard categories of wudu with proofs from Quran and companion saying.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four acts for which wudu is fard and identify the Quranic and prophetic proofs that establish their obligation.

Core Idea
Wudu is fard for prayer, touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and sajdah tilawah – each proven by a specific primary source.

In this passage, the author first classifies wudu into three types: fard, wajib, and mandub. We focus on the fard category – acts that absolutely require wudu. The author provides a Quranic verse for touching the Quran and a companion saying for funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah. Understanding the proof structure helps solidify the Hanafi view that these obligations are directly from the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts requiring fard wudu
From the passage, list the acts: (1) prayer (2) touching the Quran (3) funeral prayer (4) prostration of recitation. The text mentions these explicitly or by inference.
The passage also mentions that wudu is fard for these acts based on the proofs that follow.
2
Locate the Quranic proof for touching the Quran
Find the verse: 'None touch it except the purified' (Surah Waqiah 56:79). Understand that 'it' refers to the Quran, and 'purified' implies having wudu.
This verse is cited directly in the text.
3
Locate the companion saying for funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah
Find the report from Ibn Umar: 'A man should not prostrate except when pure... and should not pray the funeral prayer except when pure.' This is a saying of a companion, considered proof in the Hanafi school.
The text provides the full Arabic reference from Sunan Bayhaqi.
4
Understand the Hanafi classification of fard vs. wajib
Note that in the Hanafi school, these acts require wudu at the level of fard, meaning they are directly and decisively established. This is distinct from wajib, which is established by zanni evidence.
The distinction is important for understanding the hierarchy of obligations.

(۱۲۱) والثالث مندوب (۱۲۲) للنوم میں ہیں وہ بھی بغیر وضو کے جائز نہیں ہوں گی۔ (۲) قرآن کے چھونے کے بارے میں یہ آیت ہے ۔ لا يمسه الا الطهرون ۔ ( آیت ۷۹ ، سورۃ الواقعہ (۵۶) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بغیر یا کی کے قرآن کریم نہ چھوئے ۔ (۳) نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه قال لا يسجد الرجل الا وهو طاهر و لا يقرأ الا وهو طاهر و لا يصلى على الجنازة الا هو طاهر ( سنن بیہقی ، باب استحباب الظهر للذكر والقرآة ، ج اول ص ۱۴۷، نمبر ۴۲۷ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز جنازہ اور سجدہ تلاوت بغیر وضو کے نہ کرے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۰)[۲] دوسری قسم : طواف کعبہ کے لئے وضو واجب ہے۔
تشریح یہ وضو کی دوسری قسم ہے۔ کہ کعبہ کے طواف کے لئے وضو واجب ہے، کیونکہ بغیر وضو کے طواف ہو جائے گالیکن مکروہ ہے وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اور نماز میں وضو ضروری ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضوضروری ہوگا۔ اس لئے اگر بغیر وضو کے طواف قدوم کیا تو صدقہ لازم ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبى الله قال الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلوة الا انكم تتكلمون فيه فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم الا بخير ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الکلام فی الطواف ص ۱۹۰ حدیث نمبر ۹۶۰ رنسائی شریف ، باب اباحۃ الکلام فی الطواف ج ثانی ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضو شرط ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة انها قالت قدمت مكة وانا حائض ولم اطف بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة قالت فشكوت ذلك الى رسول الله فقال افعلی كما يفعل الحاج غير ان لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تطهری (بخاری شریف، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبیت ص ۲۲۳ نمبر ۱۶۵۰) اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ طہارت کے بغیر طواف نہ کرے ۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں طواف کے لئے وضوکا ذکر ہے۔ اخبرتني عائشة ان اول شيء بدأ به حين قدم أنه توضاً ثم طاف بالبيت ثم لم تكن عمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الطاف علی وضوء ، ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۶۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کر کے طواف کیا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے لئے وضو ضروری ہے۔
Section on the types of wudu. The Quran, even if one verse (120). And the second is wajib for tawaf around the Kaaba (121). And the third is mandub (122) for sleep... They are also not permissible without wudu. (2) Regarding touching the Quran, this verse: 'None touch it except the purified' (Surah Waqiah, 79). In this verse, do not touch the Quran without wudu. (3) For funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, this is a saying of a Companion: From Ibn Umar that he said: 'A man should not prostrate except when he is pure, and should not recite except when he is pure, and should not pray the funeral prayer except when he is pure' (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on desirability of purity for remembrance and Quran, vol. 1, p. 147, no. 427). In this athar, do not perform funeral prayer or prostration of recitation without wudu. Translation: (130)[2] Second type: wudu is wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba. Explanation: This is the second type of wudu. Wudu is wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba because without wudu, tawaf will occur but it is makruh. Reason: (1) In hadith, tawaf is like prayer, and wudu is necessary for prayer, so wudu is necessary for tawaf. Therefore if one performs tawaf al-qudum without wudu, sadaqah becomes obligatory. Hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it. So whoever speaks in it, let him speak only good.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on speech in tawaf, p. 190, hadith no. 960; Nasa'i, chapter on permissibility of speech in tawaf, vol. 2, p. 28, no. 2925). This hadith shows that tawaf is like prayer, so wudu is a condition for tawaf. (2) Second hadith: From Aisha that she said: 'I came to Makkah while I was menstruating, and I did not perform tawaf of the House nor between Safa and Marwah.' She said: 'I complained about that to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: Do as the pilgrim does, except that do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari, chapter on the menstruating woman performs all rites except tawaf of the House, p. 223, no. 1650). This hadith also shows that one should not perform tawaf without purity. (3) This hadith mentions wudu for tawaf: Aisha informed me that the first thing he started with when he arrived was that he performed wudu, then performed tawaf of the House, and then there was no umrah. (Bukhari, chapter on tawaf with wudu, p. 265, no. 1641). In this hadith, he performed wudu then tawaf, showing that wudu is necessary for tawaf.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof text from the chapter on types of wudu. It first classifies wudu into three categories: obligatory (fard) for prayer, touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation; required (wajib) for tawaf; and recommended (mandub) for various acts. The author provides proofs for the first two categories. For the fard category, he cites the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79) and a saying of Ibn Umar regarding funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah. These establish that touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and sajdah require wudu. For the wajib category for tawaf, he brings multiple hadith: first, the hadith 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer' (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) analogizing tawaf to prayer in requiring purity. Second, the hadith of Aisha (Bukhari) where the Prophet forbade tawaf during menstruation, indicating necessity of purity. Third, the hadith of Aisha reporting that the Prophet performed wudu before tawaf (Bukhari). These proofs show that wudu is a requirement (shart) for tawaf, though the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib rather than fard. The Urdu commentary explains that performing tawaf without wudu is valid but makruh, and if done intentionally for tawaf al-qudum, sadaqah is due.

Key Terms
وضوء (wudu): Ritual washing of hands, mouth, nose, face, arms, head, and feet with water.
فرض (fard): An obligation established by a qat'i (decisive) proof; omission without excuse makes one sinful.
طهارة (taharah): Purity; freedom from ritual impurity (hadath) and physical filth (najas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT among the acts for which wudu is fard according to the passage?
A. Prayer (salah)
B. Touching the Quran
C. Tawaf around the Kaaba
D. Funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
Wudu is fard for prayer, touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and sajdah tilawah, each proven by Quran or companion saying.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Wajib Category of Wudu for Tawaf
Classifies wudu as wajib for tawaf with three hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why wudu is wajib for tawaf in the Hanafi school and state the three hadith proofs that support this ruling.

Core Idea
Wudu is wajib for tawaf: the Prophet compared tawaf to prayer, but the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, not fard, because the hadiths are zanni, and the consequence of omission is sadaqah, not invalidation.

The second type of wudu mentioned in the passage is for tawaf around the Kaaba. The Hanafi school rules that wudu for tawaf is wajib, meaning it is required but not at the level of fard. If someone performs tawaf without wudu, the tawaf is valid but makruh, and if done intentionally for certain tawaf, a sadaqah becomes due. The author supports this with three hadiths: the comparison of tawaf to prayer, the prohibition of tawaf for a menstruating woman, and the Prophet's own practice of performing wudu before tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: wudu is wajib for tawaf
The passage explicitly states that the second type is 'wajib for tawaf around the Kaaba'. Note that this is distinct from the fard categories.
The Hanafi classification of wajib means the proof is zanni (non-decisive).
2
Examine the first hadith: 'Tawaf is like prayer'
The hadith from Ibn Abbas says tawaf is like prayer except that speech is allowed. Since prayer requires wudu, by analogy tawaf requires wudu. However, the exception (speech) indicates it is not exactly like prayer, so the obligation is only wajib.
This hadith is the primary proof.
3
Examine the second hadith: Prohibition of tawaf during menstruation
The hadith from Aisha reports that the Prophet told her not to perform tawaf until she becomes pure (from menstruation). This shows that purity is necessary for tawaf, implying wudu is required.
This is an additional indirect proof.
4
Examine the third hadith: The Prophet performed wudu before tawaf
The hadith from Aisha mentions that when the Prophet arrived in Makkah, he performed wudu then tawaf. His action is a precedent (fi'li) that indicates the requirement of wudu for tawaf.
This is a direct prophetic practice.
5
Understand the consequence of omission
The passage states that tawaf without wudu is valid but makruh (disliked). If one performs tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) without wudu, a sadaqah (charity) becomes wajib. This is the practical difference between fard and wajib.
This thamarah al-khilaf distinguishes the Hanafi view from schools that would invalidate the tawaf.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof text from the chapter on types of wudu. It first classifies wudu into three categories: obligatory (fard) for prayer, touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation; required (wajib) for tawaf; and recommended (mandub) for various acts. The author provides proofs for the first two categories. These establish that touching the Quran, funeral prayer, and sajdah require wudu. For the wajib category for tawaf, he brings multiple hadith: first, the hadith 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer' (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) analogizing tawaf to prayer in requiring purity. Second, the hadith of Aisha (Bukhari) where the Prophet forbade tawaf during menstruation, indicating necessity of purity. Third, the hadith of Aisha reporting that the Prophet performed wudu before tawaf (Bukhari). These proofs show that wudu is a requirement (shart) for tawaf, though the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib rather than fard. Key Terms
وضوء (wudu): Ritual washing of hands, mouth, nose, face, arms, head, and feet with water.
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation of a level below fard; established by a zanni proof.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but not sinful; omission is better than commission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone performs tawaf without wudu, which of the following is correct?
A. The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B. The tawaf is valid but makruh, and sadaqah may be due.
C. The tawaf is valid and no blame.
D. The person must give sadaqah regardless of the type of tawaf.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wudu for tawaf is wajib; tawaf performed without wudu is valid but makruh, and sadaqah is due for tawaf al-qudum.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
12 min
Recommended Wudu: Instances and Proofs
Lists recommended wudu occasions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on mandub wudu, list the recommended occasions, and identify the supporting proofs (hadith and athar).

Core Idea
Performing wudu for recommended occasions erases sins and brings reward, but is not obligatory.

Not every wudu is obligatory. The Hanafi school classifies many occasions where performing wudu is strongly recommended (mandub/mustahab). This lesson explores 28 such instances, focusing on those with clear textual proofs from hadith and the statements of the Salaf. Understanding these helps you earn extra reward and maintain spiritual purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category
Recognize that the author introduces a third division of wudu: mandub (recommended). Note the consequences: reward if done, no sin if omitted.
Opposite of wajib and haram.
2
List the occasions and their proofs
For the first set (sleeping with wudu, waking, continuous purity, wudu upon wudu) and the second set (after backbiting, lies, tale-bearing, any sin, bad poetry, laughter outside prayer), note the specific hadith or athar cited.
Proofs are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The common thread: wudu erases sins. Therefore, after any sin or reprehensible act, performing wudu is recommended.
This is derived from the hadith 'None maintains purity except a believer'.
4
Distinguish qahqaha inside vs outside prayer
Inside prayer, loud laughter invalidates both prayer and wudu. Outside prayer, it does not break wudu, but renewing wudu is recommended.
The hadith of the blind man falling into a well is applied to outside prayer as mustahab.

Source Text

وجه : (۱) نیند سے بیدار ہو تو وضو کرے اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قال عطاء اذا ملك الـنـوم فتوضأ قـاعـدا او مضطجعا ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الوضوء من النوم، ج اول ص ۹۸ نمبر ۴۷۵ ) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ نیند کے بعد وضو کرے۔ (۲) اور ہمیشہ باوضور ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ثوبان مولی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال قال رسول الله لا يحافظ على الطهور الا مؤمن - (مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، باب في المحافظة على الوضوء وفضله، ج اول ص ۱۴، نمبر ۳۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہمیشہ با وضور بنا مستحب ہے۔ (۳) اور وضو پر وضو کرنے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر يقول من توضأ على طهر كتب له عشرة حسنات (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی المحافظة على الوضوء وفضله، ج اول ص ۱۶، نمبر ۵۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو پر وضوکرنا دس نیکیوں کا باعث ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۲۳) [۵] اور غیبت [۶] اور جھوٹ [۷] اور چغلی ، [۸] اور ہر ایک گناہ کے بعد ، [9] اور برے اشعار پڑھنے کے بعد ، [۱۰] اور خارج نماز کے قہقہہ سے ہنسنے کے بعد ۔ تشریح : یہ سب کام ناپسندیدہ ہیں اور اس سے گناہ ہوتا ہے، اور وضو سے گناہ جھڑتے ہیں اس لئے ان کاموں کے بعد وضو کرنا مستحب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) غیبت سے وضو مستحب ہے اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الحارث قال كنت آخذ ا بيد ابراهيم فذكرت رجلا فاغتبته قال فقال لى ارجع فتوضأ ، كانوا يعدون هذا هجرا ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی الوضوء من الكلام الخبيث والغيبة ، ج اول ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۱۴۲۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ غیبت سے وضو لوٹانے کے لئے کہا۔(۲) عن ابراهیم قال اني اصلي الظهر والعصر والمغرب بوضوء واحد الا ان احدث او اقول منكرا . (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الوضوء من الکلام، ج اول ص ۹۸ نمبر (۴۷) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ جھوٹ یا غلط بات کروں تو وضو کروں۔(۳) نماز کے اندر قہقہہ لگانے سے وضو بھی ٹوٹتا ہے اور نماز بھی ٹوٹتی ہے، لیکن نماز سے باہر وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، صرف وضو کرنا مستحب ہے۔ حدیث میں
صله الله
ہے۔ عن ابی العالية ، و انس بن مالک : ان اعمی تردی فی بئر فضحك ناس خلف رسول الله عله فأمر رسـول الـلـه مـن ضحك أن يعيد الوضوء ، و الصلاة - ( دارقطنی ، باب احادیث التصقصة في الصلاة وعللها ، ج اول بص ۱۷۰، نمبر ۵۹۳ سنن بیہقی ، ، باب ترك الوضوء من القهقهة في الصلوۃ ، ج اول ،ص ۲۲۶، نمبر ۶۷۹)
Translation: (121) Third type: mustahab (recommended). Explanation: The third type of wudu is that performing wudu for it is mustahab, meaning if one does it, it is good and reward is earned, but if not, there is no difficulty. The author counted 28 actions for it. I am numbering each one. For some of them, a hadith is found so I mention it, and some issues come later for which hadith will be mentioned there. And those for which hadith was not easily found, I apologize for that. Translation: (122) (like) [1] for sleeping with wudu, [2] at the time of waking from sleep, [3] and maintaining continuous wudu, [4] and performing wudu upon wudu. Reason: (1) For waking from sleep, this athar: 'Ata said: When sleep overcomes, perform wudu sitting or lying down.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wudu from sleep, vol. 1, p. 98, no. 475). In this saying of a Tabi'i, perform wudu after sleep. (2) For maintaining continuous wudu, this hadith: From Thawban, the freed slave of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'None maintains purity except a believer.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on maintaining wudu and its virtue, vol. 1, p. 14, no. 35). In this hadith, continuously maintaining wudu is mustahab. (3) For wudu upon wudu, this hadith: From Ibn Umar who said: 'Whoever performs wudu while already in a state of purity, ten good deeds are recorded for him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on maintaining wudu and its virtue, vol. 1, p. 16, no. 53). In this hadith, performing wudu upon wudu brings ten rewards. Translation: (123) [5] After backbiting, [6] lies, [7] tale-bearing, [8] after every sin, [9] after reciting bad poetry, [10] after laughing out loud (qahqaha) outside prayer. Explanation: All these actions are disliked and cause sin, and wudu erases sins, so performing wudu after these acts is mustahab. Reason: (1) For wudu after backbiting, this athar: From al-Harith who said: I was holding Ibrahim's hand and mentioned a man and backbit him. He said to me: Go back and perform wudu. They used to consider this as abandonment (hajr). (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on wudu from evil speech and backbiting, vol. 1, p. 125, no. 1429). In this saying of a Tabi'i, he was told to return and do wudu after backbiting. (2) From Ibrahim: 'I pray Dhuhr, Asr, and Maghrib with one wudu, unless I commit a hadath or speak something objectionable.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wudu from speech, vol. 1, p. 98, no. 47). In this saying of a Tabi'i, if I lie or speak wrong, I perform wudu. (3) Laughing out loud inside prayer breaks both wudu and prayer, but outside prayer it does not break wudu; only performing wudu is mustahab. In hadith: From Abu al-Aliyah and Anas ibn Malik: A blind man fell into a well, and people laughed behind the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). So the Messenger of Allah ordered those who laughed to repeat wudu and prayer. (Darqutni, chapter on hadith of laughter in prayer and its causes, vol. 1, p. 170, no. 593; Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on leaving wudu from qahqaha in prayer, vol. 1, p. 226, no. 679).
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage continues the classification of wudu, focusing on the third category: mandub (mustahab). The author lists 28 occasions where performing wudu is recommended, not obligatory. He provides proofs for several of them. The first set includes: sleeping with wudu (so one is in a state of purity), waking from sleep, maintaining continuous wudu, and performing wudu anew even if already in wudu. For these, he cites athar from Ata (waking from sleep: perform wudu), a hadith from Thawban (only a believer maintains purity), and a hadith from Ibn Umar (ten good deeds for wudu on wudu). The second set includes: after backbiting, lying, tale-bearing, any sin, reciting bad poetry, and laughing out loud outside prayer. For backbiting, an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i instructs returning to perform wudu. For lying, a saying from Ibrahim indicates he would perform wudu if he spoke objectionably. For laughter outside prayer, a hadith about a blind man falling into a well: those who laughed were ordered to repeat wudu and prayer (though this hadith is about laughter in prayer, the author applies it to outside prayer as mustahab). The key principle: wudu erases sins, so it is recommended to perform wudu after any sin or reprehensible act.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): An action whose performance is recommended but not obligatory; omission entails no sin.
غیبة (ghibah): Backbiting: mentioning a fellow Muslim in their absence in a way they would dislike.
قہقہہ (qahqaha): Loud laughter; in prayer it breaks both prayer and wudu, but outside prayer only recommended to renew wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing wudu after backbiting?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mustahab).
C) It is forbidden (haram).
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
Wudu after sins and certain other occasions is recommended (mandub) to earn reward and erase sins, not obligatory.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Recommended Occasions for Wudu with Proofs
Lists occasions where wudu is recommended with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended occasions for wudu according to the Hanafi school and cite the specific proof (dalil) for each occasion.

Core Idea
Wudu is mustahabb (recommended) on many occasions, not wajib—the proofs are zanni (non-definitive).

This lesson expands upon a key category of wudu—the recommended occasions (masnun or mustahabb). The Hanafi school distinguishes these from obligatory (fard/wajib) occasions. While wudu is required for prayer, it is recommended at other times such as after washing the dead, before reciting Quran, or when angry. The text provides ahadith and athar to support each recommendation, helping you understand the evidentiary basis for these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasion and its ruling level
For each occasion listed, determine whether the text explicitly states the ruling (e.g., mustahabb, sunnah) or implies it through context and proofs.
The text uses terms like 'mustahabb' and 'sunnah', but check the proofs—commands (imperative) can indicate recommendation when supported by other evidence.
2
Locate the specific proof (dalil)
Find the hadith or athar cited for each occasion. Note the source (e.g., Abu Dawud, Bukhari) and the exact wording.
Some proofs are marfu' (from the Prophet) while others are mawquf (from a Sahabi) or maqtu' (from a Tabi'i).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
Explain how the command or action in the proof specifically supports recommendation rather than obligation. For example, the command 'falyatawadda' (let him perform wudu) is interpreted as nadb (recommendation) due to qara'in (contextual indicators).
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah to change it to nadb. Here, the combination of ahadith and the absence of a command for every act shows these are mustahabb.
4
Distinguish between mustahabb and wajib
Contrast these occasions with those where wudu is obligatory (e.g., for prayer). Understand that missing a recommended wudu does not invalidate the act but is considered rewarded.
The common misconception is that these are required—the text clarifies they are merely recommended.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Choose a modern scenario (e.g., attending a Zoom Quran study session) and determine whether wudu is recommended based on the principles from this text.
The occasions are analogous—if the activity involves sacred knowledge or remembrance of Allah, wudu is recommended.

وجه : عـن ابــراهيـم قـال امـض الـى عـرفـات فـاذا كان عند زوال الشمس فاغتسل ان وجدت ماء و الا فتوضا ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما ذکر فی الغسل یوم عرفہ فی الحج ، ج ثالث ص ۴۰۴، نمبر ۱۵۵۵۸) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ کے لئے غسل سنت ہے ورنہ وضو مستحب ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۲) [۲۷] اور اونٹ کے گوشت کھانے سے ۔
Chapter on the types of wudu. Backbiting and every sin, reciting poetry, and laughing loudly outside prayer (124) and washing a dead person and carrying it (125) and for the time of every prayer (126) and before ghusl of janabah (127) and for a junub when eating, drinking, sleeping, or intercourse. [Urdu definitions of words follow]. Translation: (124) [11] and after giving ghusl to the deceased and (12) after carrying the funeral. Explanation: It is mustahabb to perform wudu after that because splash may have fallen on body or clothes. Proof: (1) Hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'Whoever washes the dead, let him perform ghusl, and whoever carries it, let him perform wudu.' (2) Athar from Ibrahim: 'If it is najis, perform ghusl, otherwise wudu suffices.' Translation: (125) [13] and at the time of every prayer. Proof: Hadith from Anas: 'The Prophet used to perform wudu for each prayer unless he had broken his wudu.' Translation: (126) [14] and before ghusl of janabah. Proof: Hadith from Aisha: 'When the Prophet performed ghusl of janabah, he would start by washing his hands, then perform wudu as for prayer.' Translation: (127) [15] and for a junub when eating, drinking, sleeping, or intercourse. Proof: (1) Hadith from Aisha: 'When the Prophet wanted to eat or sleep while junub, he performed wudu.' (2) Hadith from Aisha: 'Would the Prophet sleep while junub? She said yes, after wudu.' (3) Hadith from Abu Sa'id: 'If one of you has intercourse and wants to repeat, let him perform wudu between them.' Translation: (128) [16] and at times of anger. Explanation: Perform wudu to cool anger. Translation: (129) [17] and for reciting Quran and hadith and their narration and study of sacred knowledge. Explanation: These are important sciences, so it is better to be in a state of purity. Proof: (1) Hadith from al-Muhajir ibn Qunfudh: 'The Prophet disliked mentioning Allah except in a state of purity.' (2) Athar from Ibn Umar: 'One should not recite Quran except when pure.' Translation: (130) [21] and for adhan, iqamah, and khutbah. It is mustahabb to be in purity. Proof: Hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'No one should give adhan except a mutawaddi.' Translation: (131) (24) and for visiting the Messenger of Allah, (25) standing at Arafat, (26) and sa'i between Safa and Marwah. Explanation: These are important acts of worship, so wudu is mustahabb for them. Proof: Athar from Ibrahim: 'Go to Arafat, and when the sun declines, perform ghusl if you find water, otherwise wudu.' Translation: (132) [27] and after eating camel meat.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, listing occasions on which performing wudu is recommended (mustahabb) according to the Hanafi school. The text cites ahadith and athar to support each occasion. The list includes: after washing or carrying a dead body, at the time of each prayer, before ghusl of janabah, for a junub before eating/drinking/sleeping/intercourse, during anger, before reciting Quran/hadith/studying sacred knowledge, for adhan/iqamah/khutbah, for visiting the Prophet's grave, for standing at Arafah and sa'i, and after eating camel meat. The commentary emphasizes that these are mustahabb, not obligatory, except where specified otherwise (e.g., washing a dead body requires ghusl for the washer, but wudu for the carrier). The Hanafi position is that wudu is a recommended act for these occasions, based on specific narrations. The term 'lum' (for anger) is unique.

Key Terms
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): Washing the deceased body
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed in the text as an occasion where wudu is recommended?
A) After washing a dead body
B) Before reciting Quran
C) After eating camel meat
D) Before entering the mosque

Key Takeaway
Wudu is recommended (mustahabb) on numerous occasions beyond prayer, each supported by evidence from the Sunnah.

Mustahabbat (Recommended Acts) of Wudu
Enumerates mustahab situations for wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mustahab acts of wudu listed in the Hanafi school and explain the basis for each using the proof (dalil) provided.

Core Idea
Performing wudu in certain contexts is recommended to earn reward and avoid scholarly disagreement.

This lesson presents a list of situations where the Hanafi school considers wudu to be mustahab (recommended). These include moments of anger, reciting sacred texts, giving adhan, visiting the Prophet's mosque, standing at Arafat, eating camel meat, and touching a woman. The lesson also explains the proof for each and highlights the inter-madhhab difference on touching women, encouraging the practice of ihtiyat (precaution).

Guided Path
1
Identify each act and its ruling
Go through the enumerated situations (e.g., anger, Quran recitation, adhan, etc.) and note that the ruling for performing wudu in each case is mustahab (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).
Mustahab means reward for doing, no sin for leaving.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For each act, identify the specific hadith or athar cited. For example, the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri supports wudu after intercourse, and the hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib supports wudu after camel meat.
Most proofs are ahad hadith or sayings of Companions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each proof indicates recommendation. For instance, the command 'falyatawadda' is an imperative, but in Hanafi usul a command indicates obligation unless there is a qarina (indication) for recommendation. Here, the context shows it is not obligatory.
The same imperative in Salah indicates fard, but for wudu after intercourse it is recommended because other proofs show it is not required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on touching women
The text explicitly contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. Hanafi: wudu is not broken by mere touch; Shafi'i: it is broken. The mustahab wudu here is to avoid the ikhtilaf.
This is an example of the principle 'al-khuruj min al-khilaf mustahabb'.
5
Understand the principle of ihtiyat
The lesson encourages performing wudu in uncertain cases (like touching women) to exit from disagreement, even if not obligatory. This is a common Hanafi approach.
Ihtiyat is not required, but it is meritorious.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof enumeration of mustahab (recommended) acts of wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author lists situations where performing wudu is meritorious: during anger, before reciting Quran or hadith, for adhan and khutbah, for visiting the Prophet's grave, for the rites of Hajj, after eating camel meat, and after touching a woman (to avoid ikhtilaf with Shafi'i). Each is supported by hadith or athar. The Hanafi position is that these are sunnah ghayr muakkadah; omitting them does not invalidate the act but loses reward. The section on touching a woman explicitly contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on wudu-breaking touch.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): An act recommended by the Shariah; doing it brings reward, leaving it brings no sin.
وضوء (wudu): Ritual purification of the hands, mouth, nose, face, and feet with water.
اختلاف علماء (ikhtilaf al-ulama): Disagreement among jurists on a ruling, which one may avoid by doing the precautionary action (ihtiyat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that performing wudu in specific situations (anger, Quran recitation, adhan, etc.) is recommended (mustahab), not obligatory, based on prophetic commands interpreted as recommendation, and recommends leaving ikhtilaf by performing wudu after touching women.

Wudu from Camel Meat and Touching Women: Proofs and Positions
Ruling with proof on two wudu nullifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wudu after eating camel meat and after touching a woman, and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Camel meat breaks wudu; touching a woman does not, but wudu is recommended to avoid ikhtilaf.

This passage addresses two important issues in taharah: whether eating camel meat nullifies wudu, and whether touching a woman does. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling on camel meat based on explicit hadith, but on touching women it differs from the Shafi'i school. The text explains both rulings and provides the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues and their rulings
The matn states: (1) eating camel meat breaks wudu, and (2) touching a woman prompts wudu to avoid ikhtilaf. Determine the hukm level for each.
The commentator clarifies that camel meat wudu is wajib, whereas touching women wudu is mustahabb.
2
Locate the dalil for camel meat
The proof is the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: the Prophet ordered wudu from camel meat and not from sheep meat. This explicit command indicates wujub.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from camel meat.
3
Analyze the dalil for touching women
The text cites companion sayings (Ibn 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud) that recommend wudu after kissing or touching. However, these are not taken as wajib in the Hanafi school; they are interpreted as mustahabb.
The Hanafi position is that only intercourse breaks wudu, not mere touch.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that touching a woman breaks wudu, citing Quran 4:43. The Hanafi response interprets the verse as referring to intercourse. The practical difference (thamarah) is that Hanafis do not require wudu for touch, but recommend it to avoid disagreement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi positions
The relied-upon Hanafi rulings: (1) wudu is wajib after camel meat; (2) wudu is not required after touching a woman, but it is mustahabb. These are from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

واكل لحم جزور (۱۳۳) وللخروج من خلاف العلماء كما اذا مسّ امرأة.
تشریح : اونٹ کے گوشت کھانے سے اس کی چربی کی بو آتی ہے اس لئے اس کو دفع کرنے کے لئے وضو کرنا مستحب ہے.
صلى الله
وجه : اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے . عن البراء بن عازب قال سئل رسول الله له عن الوضوء من لحوم الابل فقال توضئوا منها و سئل عن لحوم الغنم فقال لا توضئوا منها . (ابوداود شریف ، باب الوضوء من لحوم الا بل ص ۱۳۷، نمبر ۱۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اونٹ کے گوشت کھانے سے وضو کرے.

(۲) ان ابن مسعود قال : يتوضأ الرجل من المباشرة ، و من اللمس بيده ، و من القبلة اذا قبل امراته و كان يقول في هذه الآية او لامستم النساء - آیت ۴۳ ،سورة النساء ۴) قال هو الغمز ( مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الوضوء من القبلة والمس والمباشرة ، ج اول ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۴۹۹) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ بوسہ لینے سے ،عورت کو چھونے سے، اور مباشرت کرنے سے وضو کرے.
Section on nullifiers of wudu. And eating camel meat (133) and to exit from the difference of the scholars, like when he touches a woman. Explanation: From eating camel meat, its fat gives an odor, so to repel it, performing wudu is mustahabb. Proof: This hadith establishes it: from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) was asked about wudu from camel meat; he said: Perform wudu from it. And he was asked about sheep meat; he said: Do not perform wudu from it. (Abu Dawud, chapter on wudu from camel meat, p. 137, no. 184). This hadith indicates that one should do wudu after eating camel meat. Translation (133): [28] And from touching a woman etc., he should also do wudu to leave the difference of the scholars. Explanation: In the Hanafi school, wudu breaks only from intercourse, not from mere touching. And in Imam al-Shafi'i's school, wudu breaks. So to avoid this difference, doing wudu is mustahabb. Proof (1): Ibn 'Umar used to say: Whoever kisses his wife while he has wudu should repeat wudu. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wudu from kissing, touching, and direct contact, vol. 1, p. 101, no. 496). This companion's saying indicates that after kissing a woman, he should do wudu. (2) Ibn Mas'ud said: A man should do wudu from direct contact, from touching with his hand, and from kissing when he kisses his wife. And he used to say regarding this verse 'or you have touched women' (Surah al-Nisa, verse 43) - he said: it means caressing. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on wudu from kissing, touching, and direct contact, vol. 1, p. 101, no. 499). This companion's saying indicates that from kissing, touching a woman, and direct contact, he should do wudu.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on two issues: wudu from eating camel meat and from touching women. The matn states that eating camel meat breaks wudu and that to avoid disagreement with other scholars, one should also do wudu after touching a woman. The commentator explains that the Hanafi school holds wudu only from camel meat (due to hadith) and from intercourse, not from mere touch. Touching women does not break wudu in the Hanafi school; wudu after touch is only mustahabb to avoid leaving the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i who holds it breaks wudu. The proofs cited are the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib on camel meat, and the sayings of Ibn 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud on kissing and touching, which the commentator uses to show the basis for the mustahabb practice, though not the Hanafi ruling. The author follows the order of the matn, first discussing camel meat, then touching women, providing proofs for both.

Key Terms
ناقض (naqid): Something that invalidates or breaks wudu (ablution).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; omission is not sinful.
لحم جزور (lahmu jazur): Camel meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing wudu after touching a woman?
A) Wajib – touching breaks wudu
B) Mustahabb – to avoid disagreement with other schools
C) Makruh – touching is disliked
D) Haram – one should not touch a woman

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wudu is wajib after camel meat and mustahabb after touching a woman to avoid ikhtilaf.

The First Nullifier of Wudu and Its Proofs
Enumeration with proof for the first nullifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first nullifier of wudu (anything exiting from the two passages) and explain its proof from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Any impurity exiting from the front or back breaks wudu, except front wind.

This passage presents the classic Hanafi enumeration of wudu nullifiers, beginning with the most foundational: whatever exits from the two passages (urine, feces, wind, etc.). The commentator provides a detailed breakdown of specific substances and discusses an important exception: wind from the front. The proofs include the Quranic verse on tayammum and the hadith on wiping over khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifier and its exception
Read the first nullifier: 'whatever exits from the two passages, except wind from the front, in the most sound narration.' Note the exception — this is the mufta bihi position.
The exception is crucial; some other schools rule differently.
2
List the specific substances from each passage
The commentator enumerates what exits from the front (urine, madhi, wadi, mani, menstrual, postpartum, istihadah) and from the back (feces, wind, worms). This gives precision to the general ruling.
Mani is considered a nullifier here (even though it necessitates ghusl, it also breaks wudu).
3
Analyze the proof from the Quran
Examine verse 5:6: 'Or one of you comes from the toilet.' The Hanafi interpretation is that the act of relieving oneself nullifies wudu, hence any exit from the passages is a nullifier.
The proof is qat'i in transmission (Quran) but zanni in dalala, as it's an inference.
4
Analyze the proof from the hadith
The hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal permits wiping over khuffs for three days except for janabah, but includes feces, urine, and sleep. Inclusion of feces and urine indicates they nullify wudu.
This hadith is ahad in transmission but is accepted in usul as proof for rulings.
5
Distinguish front wind from actual wind
The text clarifies that a sensation of wind from the front is usually a throbbing of veins, not actual impure wind. Therefore, it does not break wudu in the relied-upon narration.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement; the other narration considered it a nullifier.

Section: Twelve things break wudu. The twelve things that break wudu at a glance: Wudu is broken by twelve things: Section on the nullifiers of wudu. Whatever exits from the two passages, except wind from the front, in the most sound narration. The birth of a child, even if blood does not appear. Impurity flowing from other than the two passages, e.g., blood and pus. ... and vomiting of food or water or congealed blood or pus mouthful. And blood that overwhelms saliva or is equal to it. ... and sleeping in such a way that the buttocks are not fixed on the ground. And the raising of the buttocks of the sleeper before waking ( from the ground in the apparent narration, even if it does not fall to the ground). ... and unconsciousness. ... and insanity. ... and intoxication. ... and the laughter of a conscious adult during prayers with bowing and prostration, even if he intends to exit from prayer by that laughter. And touching the erect penis to the private part without any barrier. Translation (134): Twelve things break wudu: [1] Whatever exits from the two passages, except wind from the front, in the most sound narration. Explanation: The author has mentioned fourteen things that break wudu. Among them, the first is that if something exits from the urethra or anus, wudu will break. The things that exit from the urethra and break wudu are: (1) urine, (2) madhi, (3) wadi, (4) mani, (5) menstrual blood, (6) postpartum blood, (7) istihadah. And these things exit from the anus: (1) feces, (2) wind, (3) intestinal worms. Wudu breaks by the exit of these ten. Sometimes a person feels that wind is exiting from the male organ or female organ; this is not wind but a throbbing of veins, so wudu does not break from it, or because this wind has no impurity. So the most sound narration is that wudu does not break from it. Proof: (1) In the verse: 'Or one of you comes from the toilet, or you have touched women, and you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 6). This verse indicates that whatever exits from the anus or urethra breaks wudu, and if there is no water, do tayammum. (2) This hadith mentions it: From Safwan ibn 'Assal: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to command us when we were on a journey not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except from janabah, but from feces, urine, and sleep. (Tirmidhi, chapter on wiping over khuffs for traveler and resident, p. 27 no. 96; Nasa'i, chapter on timing of wiping over khuffs, p. 17 no. 127). This hadith mentions that wudu breaks from janabah, feces, and urine. (3) For wudu breaking from passing wind, there is this hadith:
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof enumerating the nullifiers of wudu. The matn states that twelve things break wudu. The commentator then lists them in Urdu and Arabic, though notes that the author actually mentions fourteen. The first and most important nullifier is anything exiting from the front or back passage (urine, feces, wind, etc.), except wind from the front (which is not considered a nullifier in the sound narration). The commentator provides a detailed breakdown of substances from each passage, and distinguishes between actual wind from the rectum and false sensations. The proofs cited are: (1) Quran 5:6, which links coming from the toilet with loss of wudu, (2) the hadith of Safwan ibn 'Assal about wiping over khuffs, which excludes janabah but includes feces and urine, and (3) a hadith (incomplete) about wind. The author follows the order of the matn, first giving the list, then explaining the first item in detail.

Key Terms
سبیلین (sabīlayn): The two passages: the urethra/front passage and the anus/back passage.
اصح روایت (aṣaḥḥ al-riwāya): The most sound narration; the preferred transmission among multiple narrated opinions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on wind perceived to exit from the front passage?
A) It nullifies wudu
B) It does not nullify wudu in the most sound narration
C) It nullifies wudu only if it has odor
D) It nullifies wudu but requires istinja

Key Takeaway
The first nullifier of wudu — anything exiting from the two passages — is established by Quran and Sunnah, with the important exception of front wind in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The First Nullifier of Wudu: Whatever Exits the Two Passages
Ruling and detailed proof for nullification by exit from the two passages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification by exit from the two passages and identify which substances and exceptions apply.

Core Idea
Anything exiting the two passages nullifies wudu—except wind from the front, which is merely a sensation.

The nullifiers of wudu are central to maintaining ritual purity for prayer. This lesson examines the first and most fundamental nullifier: anything that exits the two bodily passages (urinary and fecal). You will learn the specific substances that break wudu, the exception for 'wind from the front', and the textual and rational proofs that support the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that whatever exits the two passages nullifies wudu. List the specific substances mentioned from the front and back.
Ten substances are listed; note the exception for wind from the front.
2
Apply the exception
Wind from the front (feeling of air from penis or vagina) does not nullify because it is not actual wind but a pulsation of veins. Understand the reasoning and the 'most authentic narration' behind it.
This is a Hanafi-specific distinction.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 5:6. Identify the phrase 'aw ja'a ahadun minkum min al-gha'it' and explain how it implies nullification after excretion.
The verse mentions coming from the toilet as a cause for wudu/tayammum.
4
Examine the hadith and athar proofs
Review the hadith from Safwan ibn 'Assal about not removing khuffs (shows feces/urine nullify), the hadith from Abu Hurairah defining hadath as wind, and the athar from 'Ata' about worms. Understand how each supports the general rule.
These proofs cover different types of exit.
5
Understand the rational proof
The rational argument: impurity moves from inside to outside, and any impurity reaching the body's exterior nullifies wudu. This applies even to pure substances like worms because they exit from the site of impurity.
This completes the Hanafi case.

ہیں جن سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے ۔ یہ چیزیں پیشاب کے راستے سے نکلتیں ہیں (۱) پیشاب (۲) مندی (۳) ودی (۴) منی (۵) حیض (۶) نفاس (۷) استحاضہ ۔ اور یہ چیزیں پاخانہ کے راستے سے نکلتی ہیں (۱) پاخانہ (۲) ہوا (۳) سورۃ المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں اشارہ ہے کہ پیخانہ کے راستے سے، یا پیشاب کے راستے سے جو کچھ نکلے تو اس سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا اور پانی نہ ہو تو تیم کرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں اس کا ذکر ہے۔ عن صفوان بن عسال قال كان المسح على الخفين بس ۱۷ نمبر ۱۲۷) اس حدیث میں جنابت، پیخانہ اور پیشاب سے وضو ٹوٹنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ (۳) ہوا نکلنے سے وضو ٹوٹے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے (۱۳۵) وینقضه ولادة من غير رؤية دم (۱۳۶) و نجاسة سائلة من غيرهما كدم (۱۳۷) وقيح انه سمع ابو هريرة يقول قال رسول الله لعل الله : لا تقبل صلاة من احدث حتى يتوضأ ،قال رجل من حضرموت : ما الحدث يا ابا هريرة ؟ قال فساء او ضراط ( بخاری شریف، باب لا تقبل صلاہ بغیر طهور، ص ۲۹، نمبر ۱۳۵) اس حدیث میں حدث کی تفسیر ہے کہ آواز والی ہوا یا آہستہ ہوا۔ (۴) پیخانہ کے کیڑے سے وضوٹوٹے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ قال عطاء : فيمن يخرج من دبره الدودة ، او من ذكره نحو القملة : يعيد الوضوء ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب من لم يرا لوضوء الا من الحجر جین من القبل والد بر ص ۳۵ نمبر ۱۷۶) اس اثر سے پتہ چلا کہ ان دونوں راستوں سے جو کچھ بھی نکلے اس سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ (۵) دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ۔ یہ دونوں مقام مقام نجاست نہیں ہیں۔ نجاست کہیں اوپر سے کھسک کر آتی ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کوئی ناپا کی اپنی جگہ سے کھسک کر جسم کے ظاہری حصے پر آجائے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔اس لئے ان چیزوں سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
Section on the nullifiers of wudu. (134) Whatever exits the two passages except wind from the front, according to the most authentic view. And blood that dominates or equals saliva. ... and sleeping in a way that the buttocks are not settled on the ground. And before waking, the buttocks of the sleeper lifting (from the ground, according to the apparent narration even if it does not fall on the ground). ... and unconsciousness. ... and insanity. and intoxication (nashwa). ... and laughing with a loud ha-ha in a prayer with bowing and prostration while awake and adult, even if he intends to exit from the prayer by that laughter. And touching the standing penis with the hand without a barrier. Translation: (134) Twelve things break wudu: [1] Whatever exits the two passages except wind from the front, according to the most authentic narration. Explanation: The author has mentioned fourteen things here that nullify wudu. Among them, the first is that if something exits from the urinary or fecal passage, wudu is nullified. The following things exit from the urinary passage: (1) urine, (2) madhi (pre-seminal fluid), (3) wadi (prostatic fluid), (4) mani (semen), (5) menstrual blood, (6) postpartum blood, (7) istihadah (non-menstrual uterine bleeding). And these things exit from the fecal passage: (1) feces, (2) wind, (3) intestinal worms. By the exit of these ten, wudu is nullified. Sometimes one feels that wind is exiting from a man's penis or a woman's private part; that is not wind but rather a pulsation of veins, so wudu is not broken by that, or there is no impurity in that wind, so the most authentic narration is that wudu is not nullified by it. Proof: (1) The verse says: 'Or one of you comes from the toilet or touched women and find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6). This verse indicates that whatever exits from the fecal or urinary passage nullifies wudu, and if no water is available, perform tayammum. (2) This hadith mentions it: From Safwan ibn 'Assal: The Messenger of Allah (saw) used to command us, when we were traveling, not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except from janabah, but from feces, urine, and sleep (Tirmidhi, Bab al-Mash 'ala al-Khuffayn, p. 27, no. 96; Nasa'i, Bab al-Tawqit fi al-Mash 'ala al-Khuffayn, p. 17, no. 127). This hadith mentions nullification from janabah, feces, and urine. (3) For nullification by wind, this hadith is: (135) And it nullifies by birth without seeing blood. (136) And by liquid impurity from other than them like blood. (137) And pus. That he heard Abu Hurairah say: The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of one who had a hadath until he performs wudu.' A man from Hadramawt asked: 'What is hadath, O Abu Hurairah?' He said: 'Fart or wind.' (Bukhari, Bab La Tuqbal Salat Bighayr Tuhur, p. 29, no. 135) This hadith explains hadath: loud wind or soft wind. (4) For nullification by intestinal worms, this is the saying of a Tabi'i: 'Ata said: For one from whose anus a worm exits, or from his penis something like a louse: he should repeat wudu.' (Bukhari, Bab Man Lam Yara al-Wudu Illa min al-Hajarayn, p. 35, no. 176) This athar shows that whatever exits from these two passages nullifies wudu. (5) The rational proof is that these two places are not places of impurity; impurity comes from above by moving. And the rule is: if any impurity moves from its place to an apparent part of the body, wudu is nullified. Therefore, wudu is nullified by these things.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the first nullifier of wudu: anything exiting the two passages (anterior and posterior). The author lists ten specific substances: from the front: urine, madhi, wadi, mani, menstrual blood, postpartum blood, istihadah; from the back: feces, wind, and intestinal worms. The exception is wind from the front (feeling of air from the penis or vagina) which is not actual wind but a sensation, so it does not nullify wudu according to the most authentic narration. The proofs include Quran 5:6, which implies nullification by excretion; a hadith from Safwan ibn 'Assal about not removing khuffs except for janabah, feces, urine, and sleep; a hadith from Abu Hurairah defining hadath as fart or wind; and a saying of 'Ata' regarding worms. A rational proof is also given: these passages are not inherently impure, but impurity moving from inside to the outer body nullifies wudu. This is a typical Hanafi presentation combining textual and rational evidence.

Key Terms
نواقض الوضوء (nawaqid al-wudu): Things that nullify the state of ritual purity (wudu).
سبيلين (sabilayn): The two passages: the urethra (urine/birth canal) and the anus.
ريح القبل (reeh al-qabl): Wind from the front (penis or vagina) – a sensation that does not nullify wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT nullify wudu when exiting from the two passages?
A) Wind from the anus
B) Wind from the front (penis/vagina)
C) A small worm from the anus
D) Urine

Key Takeaway
The first nullifier of wudu is anything exiting the two passages, with the sole exception of wind from the front which is not true wind.

Nullification by Liquid Impurity from Non-Passage Areas
Ruling that liquid impurity from other than the two passages nullifies wudu if it flows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification by liquid impurity from non-passage areas and apply the condition of flow to determine whether wudu is nullified.

Core Idea
From other than the two passages, liquid impurity nullifies wudu only if it flows.

In the previous lesson, we learned that any exit from the two passages (front and back) nullifies wudu, regardless of quantity or impurity. Now we turn to other parts of the body: a cut, a wound, a pimple. The ruling here is different: the substance must be both impure (najis) and in a quantity that flows. This distinction is a hallmark of the Hanafi school and prevents unnecessary invalidation from minor non-flowing impurities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the exiting substance
Determine whether the substance exits from the two passages (urethra/anüs) or from elsewhere (e.g., skin, nose, ear). If from the two passages, the previous ruling applies: any amount nullifies, impure or not.
This step distinguishes the two main categories of nullifiers.
2
Check if the substance is impure (najis)
If the substance is not impure (e.g., tears, sweat, phlegm, saliva), wudu is not nullified regardless of quantity. Only impure substances such as blood, pus, or yellow fluid are candidates for nullification.
Pure liquids like water or tears do not nullify.
3
Check if the substance is liquid and flows
Even if the substance is impure, it must be liquid and flow from the exit point. A static drop that does not spread or run does not nullify wudu. The Hanafi school defines 'flow' as the substance moving from the spot of exit.
A small amount of blood that remains beaded without running does not nullify.
4
Derive the ruling
If both conditions (impurity + flow) are met, wudu is nullified. If either condition is absent, wudu remains valid.
This ruling is based on the principle that the two passages are special due to their nature; other exits require additional conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۶) [۳] پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے کے علاوہ سے کوئی بہنے والی نجاست ہو، جیسے خون اور پیپ [ تو اس سے بھی وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا ] تشریح : پیخانہ اور پیشاب کے راستے کے بارے میں یہ تھا کہ تھوڑی سی بھی کوئی چیز ظاہر ہو تو چاہے وہ بہے یا نہیں، اور نجاست ہو یا نہ ہو تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جائے گا۔ لیکن انکے علاوہ کا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکلنے والی چیز نجاست ہو، اور اتنی ہو کہ جسم پر بہہ پڑے تب وضو ٹوٹے گا۔ اگر نکلنے والی چیز نجاست نہیں ہے، مثلا بلغم ہے تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا، یا نجاست ہے لیکن اتنی مقدار نہیں ہے کہ بہہ سکے تو وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔
Translation: (136) [3] From other than the fecal and urinary passages, any liquid impurity, such as blood and pus [then that also nullifies wudu]. Explanation: Regarding the fecal and urinary passages, it was that if even a little something appears, whether it flows or not, and whether it is impure or not, then wudu is nullified. But the rule for other than them is that the exiting thing must be impure, and it must be in a quantity that flows on the body; then wudu is nullified. If the exiting thing is not impure, such as phlegm, then wudu is not nullified. Or if it is impure but not enough to flow, then wudu is not nullified.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents the third nullifier: liquid impurity (like blood, pus) flowing from parts other than the two passages. The author distinguishes this from the previous rule. For the two passages, even a tiny amount, whether impure or not, nullifies wudu. For other parts of the body, the substance must be impure (najis) AND must flow (be in a quantity that runs). If it is not impure (e.g., tears, sweat, phlegm) or if it is impure but does not flow (a drop that does not spread), wudu is not nullified. The ruling is based on the principle that impurity exiting the body from other places is treated similarly to that from the two passages but with the additional condition of flowing quantity, as established by analogy and practice.

Key Terms
نجاسة سائلة (najasa sā'ila): Liquid impurity, such as blood or pus, that flows from the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has a small cut on his finger that produces a drop of blood that does not flow. According to the Hanafi school:
A) His wudu is nullified because blood is najis.
B) His wudu is not nullified because the blood did not flow.
C) His wudu is nullified only if the blood is from the two passages.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
For wudu nullification from non-passage areas, the impurity must be both najis and flowing; a non-flowing drop does not break wudu.

General Nullifiers: Anything Exiting the Two Passages
Explanation of the hadith and rational proof for the nullification of wudu by any exit from the two passages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule that any exit from the two passages nullifies wudu, and support it with the hadith of Abu Hurairah and a rational proof.

Core Idea
Anything exiting the two passages breaks wudu — even dry wind or a worm — because 'hadath' is not limited to impure substances.

Wudu is nullified by certain events (hadath). The most fundamental nullifier is anything that exits from the front or back passage. In this lesson, we examine the proof for this rule from a famous hadith and the rational extension (qiyas) that covers all exits, regardless of impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nullifier and its ruling
The act in question is the exit of any substance from the two passages. According to the Hanafi school, this nullifies wudu, making it necessary to renew.
2
Locate the hadith dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) states that prayer is not accepted from one who has hadath until he performs wudu. Abu Hurairah explains hadath as a fart or silent wind.
Hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 135.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation of acceptance (la tuqbal) indicates that wudu is a prerequisite. The term 'hadath' is interpreted as any event from the two passages, as per the explanation of the Companion.
4
Note the subsidiary ruling and rational proof
The author adds that even a worm exiting the anus or penis breaks wudu, citing the statement of 'Ata. Then a rational proof is given: the two passages are places where impurities exit, and when impurity (or anything) shifts from inside to the external body, wudu breaks.
The rational proof is a qiyas based on the principle of impurity shifting.
5
Formulate the general principle
Thus, the general rule is: any substance, impure or not, exiting the two passages nullifies wudu. This includes gas, feces, urine, worms, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في نواقض الوضوء (۱۳۵) وینقضه ولادة من غير رؤية دم (۱۳۶) و نجاسة سائلة من غيرهما كدم (۱۳۷) وقيح انه سمع ابو هريرة يقول قال رسول الله لعل الله : لا تقبل صلاة من احدث حتى يتوضأ ،قال رجل من حضرموت : ما الحدث يا ابا هريرة ؟ قال فساء او ضراط ( بخاری شریف، باب لا تقبل صلاہ بغیر طهور، ص ۲۹، نمبر ۱۳۵) اس حدیث میں حدث کی تفسیر ہے کہ آواز والی ہوا یا آہستہ ہوا. (۴) پیخانہ کے کیڑے سے وضوٹوٹے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ قال عطاء : فيمن يخرج من دبره الدودة ، او من ذكره نحو القملة : يعيد الوضوء ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب من لم يرا لوضوء الا من الحجر جین من القبل والد بر ص ۳۵ نمبر ۱۷۶) اس اثر سے پتہ چلا کہ ان دونوں راستوں سے جو کچھ بھی نکلے اس سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ (۵) دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ۔ یہ دونوں مقام مقام نجاست نہیں ہیں۔ نجاست کہیں اوپر سے کھسک کر آتی ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کوئی ناپا کی اپنی جگہ سے کھسک کر جسم کے ظاہری حصے پر آجائے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے۔اس لئے ان چیزوں سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔
Chapter on the Nullifiers of Ablution. (135) Childbirth without seeing blood nullifies it. (136) Flowing impurity from other than them, like blood and pus. (137) [Vomit] ... He heard Abu Hurairah say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Prayer is not accepted from one who has hadath until he performs ablution.' A man from Hadhramaut asked: 'What is hadath, O Abu Hurairah?' He said: 'Fart or silent wind.' (Bukhari, chapter: Prayer is not accepted without purification, p.29, no.135). In this hadith, hadath is explained as audible wind or silent wind. (4) Wudu breaks from worms of the anus. For this is the statement of a tabi'i. 'Ata said: Regarding one from whose anus a worm comes out, or from his penis something like a louse: he should repeat the wudu.' (Bukhari, chapter: Whoever did not consider wudu necessary except from the two passages, front and back, p.35, no.176). From this athar it is understood that whatever exits from these two passages will break wudu. (5) The rational proof is that these two places are not places of impurity. Impurity comes shifting from above. And the rule is that when any impurity shifts from its place and comes to the external part of the body, then wudu breaks. Therefore wudu breaks from these things.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an opening of the chapter on nullifiers of wudu. It begins by listing the nullifiers in numerical form: childbirth without seeing blood (135), flowing impurity from other than the two passages like blood and pus (136), and vomiting (137) – though the text of the matn is incomplete at this point. The author then immediately provides a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet (peace be upon him) states that prayer is not accepted from one who has 'hadath' until he performs wudu. Abu Hurairah explains 'hadath' as a fart or silent wind. This establishes that any emission from the two passages, whether with sound or not, is a nullifier. The author then adds a subsidiary ruling: that worms exiting the anus or penis break wudu, citing a statement of 'Ata. This shows that anything exiting the two passages, even if not typical impurity, breaks wudu. The author then provides a rational proof: the two passages are not inherently impure; impurity comes from inside and when it reaches the external body, it breaks wudu. Hence the general principle is that any substance, impure or not, exiting the two passages nullifies wudu.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): The state of ritual impurity specifically caused by an event (exiting from the two passages) that invalidates wudu.
سبیلین (sabilayn): The two passages: front (penis/vagina) and back (anus).
نواقض الوضوء (nawaqid al-wudu): Things that break or invalidate wudu, requiring its renewal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what did Abu Hurairah identify as 'hadath' that breaks wudu?
A) Only liquid impurities
B) Audible or silent wind from the anus
C) Urine and feces
D) Blood and pus

Key Takeaway
Any exit from the two passages, whether impure or not, nullifies wudu.

Childbirth Nullifies Wudu Even Without Blood
Ruling with proof: childbirth nullifies wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on childbirth as a nullifier of wudu and explain the evidence from the hadith 'al-wudu' mimma kharaja'.

Core Idea
Childbirth nullifies wudu without blood because any exit from the private part breaks it.

Many assume wudu breaks only when blood is seen after childbirth, but the Hanafi ruling is broader. This lesson unpacks the hadith and reasoning that establishes childbirth itself — even without visible blood — as a wudu nullifier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the passage addresses childbirth (wiladah) and rules that it nullifies wudu, making renewal of wudu obligatory before prayer.
The ruling applies regardless of whether blood is seen.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'al-wudu' mimma kharaja wa laysa mimma dakhala' (wudu is due to what exits, not what enters). Identify it as an ahad hadith with zanni thubut.
Hadith reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand that 'what exits' includes any object or fluid from the two private parts. Childbirth is an exit, so it triggers the ruling. The principle is: any exit, little or much, impure or not, nullifies wudu.
This is a general Hanafi usul rule applied to a specific case.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools limit nullification to substances that are impure (najis) or to blood specifically. The Hanafi school holds a broader view based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.
This difference has practical consequences for postpartum women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۵) بچہ کا پیدا ہونا، اگر چہ خون ظاہر نہ ہو۔ تشریح : بچہ پیدا ہونے کے ساتھ خون آجائے تب تو عورت نفاس والی ہو گئی اس لئے اس نفاس سے وضو ٹوٹے گا لیکن خون نظر نہ آئے تب بھی صرف بچہ نکلنے سے بھی وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) بچہ جب بھی نکلے گا تو خون کے علاوہ بھی اس پر شرمگاہ کی نجاست ہوگی اس لئے اس نجاست کے نکلنے سے وضو ٹوٹے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ شرمگاہ سے کوئی بھی چیز نکلے تو اس سے وضو ٹوٹے گا اس لئے صرف بچہ پیدا ہونے سے بھی وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا ۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الا الله قال الوضوء مما خرج و ليس مما دخل ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب الوضوء من الدم يخرج من احد السبيلين وغير ذالك من دورة او حصاة او غير ذالک ، ج اول ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۶۸ ۱۵ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من یطاء نتایا بسا اور طبا ، ج اول ص ۲۴ نمبر ۱۰۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سبیلین سے کوئی چیز نکلے تو اس سے وضوٹوٹے گا۔ اصول : سبیلین سے نکلنے والی چیز تھوڑی ہو یا زیادہ ، نجاست ہو یا نہ ہو ناقض وضو ہے۔
Translation of (135): Childbirth, even if blood does not appear. Explanation: If blood accompanies childbirth, then the woman is in nifas, so wudu breaks due to nifas. But if no blood is seen, still merely the birth of the child breaks wudu. Reason: (1) Whenever the child exits, there will be impurity from the vagina besides blood, so wudu breaks due to that impurity. (2) There is a hadith that if anything exits from the private part, wudu breaks, so simply childbirth breaks wudu. The hadith is: From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Wudu is due to what exits, not what enters.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on wudu from blood exiting from one of the two passages, and other things like worm or pebble, etc., vol.1 p.188 no.68; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, vol.1 p.24 no.100). In this hadith, if anything exits from the two passages, wudu breaks. Principle: Whatever exits from the two passages, whether little or much, impure or not, is a nullifier of wudu.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a specific ruling on childbirth as a nullifier. The author explains that even if no blood is seen, childbirth itself breaks wudu. Two reasons are given: first, the child brings with it vaginal impurities; second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas states that wudu is due to what exits, not what enters. The author then states the general principle: anything exiting the two passages, regardless of quantity or impurity, nullifies wudu. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that all exits from the front and back passages are nullifiers.

Key Terms
ولادة (wiladah): Childbirth, the act of giving birth.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding; its presence causes a separate state of ritual impurity.
سبیلین (sabilayn): The two passages: front (urinary/vaginal) and back (anal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does childbirth without blood still nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because blood is always present even if invisible
B) Because any exit from the private part nullifies wudu
C) Because the child is impure
D) Because of the hadith that blood nullifies wudu

Key Takeaway
Childbirth nullifies wudu even without blood because the Hanafi school applies the general hadith that any exit from the private parts breaks wudu.
